      <p><b>Botswana</b> (<span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="'b' in 'buy'">b</span><span title="/ɒ/: 'o' in 'body'">ɒ</span><span title="'t' in 'tie'">t</span><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'s' in 'sigh'">s</span><span title="'w' in 'wind'">w</span><span title="/ɑː/: 'a' in 'father'">ɑː</span><span title="'n' in 'nigh'">n</span><span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">ə</span></span>/</a></span> <span class="nowrap" style="font-size:85%">(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap;margin-right:.25em;"><a href="/wiki/File:En-Bostwana-pronunciation.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" decoding="async" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20"></a></span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/d/d4/En-Bostwana-pronunciation.ogg" class="internal" title="En-Bostwana-pronunciation.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</span></span>, <small>also</small> <span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><small><a href="/wiki/British_English" title="British English">UK</a>: </small><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="'b' in 'buy'">b</span><span title="/ʊ/: 'u' in 'push'">ʊ</span><span title="'t' in 'tie'">t</span></span>-,<span class="wrap"> </span><span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="'b' in 'buy'">b</span><span title="/ʊ/: 'u' in 'push'">ʊ</span><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="/tʃ/: 'ch' in 'China'">tʃ</span><span title="'w' in 'wind'">w</span></span>-/</a></span></span><sup id="cite_ref-Collins_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Collins-15">[15]</a></sup>), officially the <b>Republic of Botswana</b> (<a href="/wiki/Setswana" class="mw-redirect" title="Setswana">Setswana</a>: <i lang="tn">Lefatshe la Botswana</i>; <a href="/wiki/Kalanga_language" title="Kalanga language">Kalanga</a>: <i>Hango yeBotswana</i>), is a <a href="/wiki/Landlocked_country" title="Landlocked country">landlocked country</a> in <a href="/wiki/Southern_Africa" title="Southern Africa">Southern Africa</a>. Botswana is topographically flat, with up to 70 percent of its territory being the <a href="/wiki/Kalahari_Desert" title="Kalahari Desert">Kalahari Desert</a>. It is bordered by <a href="/wiki/South_Africa" title="South Africa">South Africa</a> to the south and southeast, <a href="/wiki/Namibia" title="Namibia">Namibia</a> to the west and north, and <a href="/wiki/Zimbabwe" title="Zimbabwe">Zimbabwe</a> to the northeast. Its border with <a href="/wiki/Zambia" title="Zambia">Zambia</a> to the north near <a href="/wiki/Kazungula,_Zambia" class="mw-redirect" title="Kazungula, Zambia">Kazungula</a> is poorly defined due to being in the midst of the Zambezi River. This border with Zambia is, at most, a few hundred metres long.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>A mid-sized country of just over 2.3 million people, it is one of the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_population_density" class="mw-redirect" title="List of countries by population density">most sparsely populated</a> countries in the world. About 10 percent of the population lives in the capital and largest city, <a href="/wiki/Gaborone" title="Gaborone">Gaborone</a>. Formerly one of the world's poorest countries—with a GDP per capita of about US$70 per year in the late 1960s—Botswana has since transformed itself into an upper middle income country, with one of the world's fastest-growing economies.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><i><a href="/wiki/Homo_sapiens" class="mw-redirect" title="Homo sapiens">Homo sapiens</a></i> had first inhabited the country over 200,000 years ago. The <a href="/wiki/Tswana_people" title="Tswana people">Tswana ethnic group</a> were descended mainly from <a href="/wiki/Bantu_peoples" title="Bantu peoples">Bantu-speaking tribes</a> who migrated southward of Africa to modern Botswana around 600 AD, living in tribal enclaves as farmers and herders. In 1885, the <a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">British</a> colonized the area and declared a <a href="/wiki/Protectorate" title="Protectorate">protectorate</a> under the name of <a href="/wiki/Bechuanaland_Protectorate" title="Bechuanaland Protectorate">Bechuanaland</a>. As <a href="/wiki/Decolonization_of_Africa" class="mw-redirect" title="Decolonization of Africa">decolonization occurred</a>, Bechuanaland became an independent <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">Commonwealth</a> republic under its current name on 30 September 1966.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> Since then, it has been a <a href="/wiki/Representative_republic" class="mw-redirect" title="Representative republic">representative republic</a>, with a consistent record of uninterrupted democratic <a href="/wiki/Elections_in_Botswana" title="Elections in Botswana">elections</a> and the lowest perceived corruption ranking in Africa since at least 1998.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The economy is dominated by <a href="/wiki/Mining_industry_of_Botswana" title="Mining industry of Botswana">mining</a>, cattle, and <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Botswana" title="Tourism in Botswana">tourism</a>. Botswana has a GDP (<a href="/wiki/Purchasing_power_parity" title="Purchasing power parity">purchasing power parity</a>) per capita of about $18,825 per year as of 2015<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Botswana&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, one of the highest in Africa.<sup id="cite_ref-cia_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia-1">[1]</a></sup> Its high <a href="/wiki/Gross_national_income" title="Gross national income">gross national income</a> (by some estimates the fourth-largest in Africa) gives the country a relatively high standard of living and the highest <a href="/wiki/Human_Development_Index" title="Human Development Index">Human Development Index</a> of continental <a href="/wiki/Sub-Saharan_Africa" title="Sub-Saharan Africa">Sub-Saharan Africa</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Botswana is a member of the <a href="/wiki/African_Union" title="African Union">African Union</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Southern_African_Development_Community" title="Southern African Development Community">Southern African Development Community</a>, the Commonwealth of Nations, and the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a>. The country has been adversely affected by the <a href="/wiki/HIV/AIDS_in_Botswana" title="HIV/AIDS in Botswana">HIV/AIDS epidemic</a>. Despite the success in programmes to make treatments available, and to educate the populace about how to stop the spread of HIV/AIDS, the number of people with AIDS rose from 290,000 in 2005 to 320,000 in 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-Gap_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gap-21">[21]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>A20</span></sup> As of 2014<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Botswana&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, Botswana has the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_HIV/AIDS_adult_prevalence_rate" title="List of countries by HIV/AIDS adult prevalence rate">third-highest prevalence rate</a> for HIV/AIDS, with roughly 20% of the population infected.<sup id="cite_ref-Avert_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Avert-22">[22]</a></sup> </p>

          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-25"><a href="#Music"><span class="tocnumber">7.3</span> <span class="toctext">Music</span></a></li>

           <ul>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Botswana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <p>The country's name means "Land of the <a href="/wiki/Tswana_people" title="Tswana people">Tswana</a>", referring to the dominant <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_groups_in_Botswana" title="Ethnic groups in Botswana">ethnic group in Botswana</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> The term <i>Batswana</i> was originally applied to the Tswana, which is still the case.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> However, it has also come to be used generally as a <a href="/wiki/Demonym" title="Demonym">demonym</a> for all citizens of Botswana.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> Many <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English</a> dictionaries also include <i>Botswanan</i> to refer to people of Botswana, though that term is rarely used in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Botswana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Botswana" title="History of Botswana">History of Botswana</a>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_history">Early history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Botswana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Early history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Two_Rhino.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Two_Rhino.jpg/220px-Two_Rhino.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Two_Rhino.jpg/330px-Two_Rhino.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Two_Rhino.jpg/440px-Two_Rhino.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2000" data-file-height="1339"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Two_Rhino.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The 'Two Rhino' painting at <a href="/wiki/Tsodilo" title="Tsodilo">Tsodilo</a>,a <a href="/wiki/UNESCO_World_Heritage_Site" class="mw-redirect" title="UNESCO World Heritage Site">UNESCO World Heritage Site</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Archaeological digs have shown that hominids have lived in Botswana for around two million years. Stone tools and fauna remains have shown that all areas of the country were inhabited at least 400,000 years ago.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> In October 2019, researchers reported that Botswana was the birthplace of all <a href="/wiki/Anatomically_modern_humans" class="mw-redirect" title="Anatomically modern humans">modern humans</a> about 200,000 years ago.<sup id="cite_ref-NAT-20191028_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NAT-20191028-28">[28]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><sup id="cite_ref-SA-20191028_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SA-20191028-29">[29]</a></sup> Evidence left by modern humans such as cave paintings are about 73,000 years old.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> The original inhabitants of southern Africa were the Bushmen (<a href="/wiki/San_people" title="San people">San</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Khoi" class="mw-redirect" title="Khoi">Khoi</a> peoples. Both speak <a href="/wiki/Khoisan_languages" title="Khoisan languages">Khoisan languages</a> and hunted, gathered, and traded over long distances. When cattle were first introduced about 2000 years ago into southern Africa, pastoralism became a major feature of the economy, since the region had large grasslands free of <a href="/wiki/Tsetse_fly" title="Tsetse fly">tsetse fly</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> </p> 
      <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r978413945/mw-parser-output/.tmulti">.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbinner{display:flex;flex-direction:column}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow{display:flex;flex-direction:row;clear:left;flex-wrap:wrap;width:100%;box-sizing:border-box}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{margin:1px;float:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .theader{clear:both;font-weight:bold;text-align:center;align-self:center;background-color:transparent;width:100%}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbcaption{background-color:transparent}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-left{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-right{text-align:right}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-center{text-align:center}@media all and (max-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbinner{width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;max-width:none!important;align-items:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow{justify-content:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{float:none!important;max-width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle .thumbcaption{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow>.thumbcaption{text-align:center}}</style>
      <div class="thumb tmulti tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:204px;max-width:204px">
        <div class="trow">
         <div class="tsingle" style="width:202px;max-width:202px">
          <div class="thumbimage">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Domboshaba_stone_wall_3.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Domboshaba_stone_wall_3.jpg/200px-Domboshaba_stone_wall_3.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="133" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Domboshaba_stone_wall_3.jpg/300px-Domboshaba_stone_wall_3.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Domboshaba_stone_wall_3.jpg/400px-Domboshaba_stone_wall_3.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5184" data-file-height="3456"></a>
          </div>
         </div>
        </div>
        <div class="trow">
         <div class="tsingle" style="width:202px;max-width:202px">
          <div class="thumbimage">
           <a href="/wiki/File:The_plate_that_was_used_in_the_past_at_Domboshaba_monument.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/The_plate_that_was_used_in_the_past_at_Domboshaba_monument.jpg/200px-The_plate_that_was_used_in_the_past_at_Domboshaba_monument.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="133" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/The_plate_that_was_used_in_the_past_at_Domboshaba_monument.jpg/300px-The_plate_that_was_used_in_the_past_at_Domboshaba_monument.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/The_plate_that_was_used_in_the_past_at_Domboshaba_monument.jpg/400px-The_plate_that_was_used_in_the_past_at_Domboshaba_monument.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5184" data-file-height="3456"></a>
          </div>
          <div class="thumbcaption">
           <a href="/wiki/Domboshaba" title="Domboshaba">Domboshaba</a> Ruins Stone Wall (top) and clay pottery plate (bottom).
          </div>
         </div>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>It is unclear when <a href="/wiki/Bantu_languages" title="Bantu languages">Bantu</a>-speaking peoples first moved into the country from the north, although AD 600 seems to be a consensus estimate. In that era, the ancestors of the modern-day <a href="/wiki/Kalanga_people" title="Kalanga people">Kalanga</a> moved into what is now the north-eastern areas of the country. These proto-Kalanga were closely connected to states in <a href="/wiki/Zimbabwe" title="Zimbabwe">Zimbabwe</a> as well as to the <a href="/wiki/Mapungubwe" class="mw-redirect" title="Mapungubwe">Mapungubwe</a> state and the notable of these was <a href="/wiki/Domboshaba" title="Domboshaba">Domboshaba</a> ruins which is a cultural and heritage site in Botswana originally occupied towards the end of the Great Zimbabwe period (1250–1450 AD) with stone walls that have an average height of 1.8 metres. The site is a respected place for the people living in the region and it is believed that the chief lived on the top of the hill together with his helpers or assistants. These states, located outside of current Botswana's borders, appear to have kept massive cattle herds in what is now the Central District—apparently at numbers approaching modern cattle density.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> This massive cattle-raising complex prospered until 1300 AD or so, and seems to have regressed following the collapse of Mapungubwe. During this era, the first Tswana-speaking groups, the <a href="/wiki/Bakgalagadi" class="mw-redirect" title="Bakgalagadi">Bakgalagadi</a>, moved into the southern areas of the <a href="/wiki/Kalahari" class="mw-redirect" title="Kalahari">Kalahari</a>. All these various peoples were connected to trade routes that ran via the Limpopo River to the Indian Ocean, and trade goods from Asia such as beads made their way to Botswana most likely in exchange for ivory, gold, and <a href="/wiki/Rhinoceros_horn" class="mw-redirect" title="Rhinoceros horn">rhinoceros horn</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Toutswemogala_Hill" title="Toutswemogala Hill">Toutswemogala Hill</a> Iron Age Settlement's radio-carbon dates for this settlement range from 7th to late 19th century AD indicating occupation of more than one thousand years. The hill was part of the formation of early states in Southern Africa with cattle keeping as major source of economy. Toutswe settlement include house-floors, large heaps of vitrified cow-dog and burials while the outstanding structure is the stone wall. There are large tracts of centaurs ciliaris, a type of grass which has come to be associated with cattle-keeping settlements in South, Central Africa.Around 700 A.D., the <a href="/wiki/Toutswe" class="mw-redirect" title="Toutswe">Toutswe</a> people moved westward into Botswana and began an agricultural and pastoral land tenure system based on <a href="/wiki/Sorghum" title="Sorghum">sorghum</a> and <a href="/wiki/Millet" title="Millet">millet</a>, and domesticated stock, respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-Hall_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hall-34">[34]</a></sup> The site was situated in the center of a broader cultural area in Eastern Botswana and shares many commonalities with other archaeological sites of this region, in both ceramic production styles and also timeframes inhabited.<sup id="cite_ref-Hall_34-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hall-34">[34]</a></sup> Large structures were observed that contained vitrified remains of animal dung, leading to the theory that these were animal enclosures and that Toutswemogala Hill was thus a major center of animal husbandry in the region.<sup id="cite_ref-Hall_34-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hall-34">[34]</a></sup> However, agriculture also played a vital role in the longevity of Toutswemogala Hill's extended occupation, as many grain storage structures have also been found on the site. Many different stratified layers of housing floors further signal continuous occupation over hundreds of years. </p>
      <p>The arrival of the ancestors of the Tswana-speakers who came to control the region has yet to be dated precisely. Members of the <a href="/wiki/Bakwena" class="mw-redirect" title="Bakwena">Bakwena</a>, a chieftaincy under a legendary leader named Kgabo II, made their way into the southern Kalahari by AD 1500, at the latest, and his people drove the Bakgalagadi inhabitants west into the desert. Over the years, several offshoots of the Bakwena moved into adjoining territories. The <a href="/wiki/Bangwaketse" title="Bangwaketse">Bangwaketse</a> occupied areas to the west, while the <a href="/wiki/Bangwato" class="mw-redirect" title="Bangwato">Bangwato</a> moved northeast into formerly Kalanga areas.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> Not long afterwards, a Bangwato offshoot known as the Batawana migrated into the Okavango Delta, probably in the 1790s.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Effects_of_the_Mfecane_and_Batswana-Boer_Wars">Effects of the Mfecane and Batswana-Boer Wars</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Botswana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Effects of the Mfecane and Batswana-Boer Wars">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Mfecane" title="Mfecane">Mfecane</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Kapstaaten_1905.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Kapstaaten_1905.png/220px-Kapstaaten_1905.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="224" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Kapstaaten_1905.png/330px-Kapstaaten_1905.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Kapstaaten_1905.png/440px-Kapstaaten_1905.png 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="1016"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Kapstaaten_1905.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>German map of 1905 still showing the undivided Bechuanaland area
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The first written records relating to modern-day Botswana appear in 1824. What these records show is that the Bangwaketse had become the predominant power in the region. Under the rule of Makaba II, the Bangwaketse kept vast herds of cattle in well-protected desert areas, and used their military prowess to raid their neighbours.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> Other chiefdoms in the area, by this time, had capitals of 10,000 or so and were fairly prosperous.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> This equilibrium came to end during the <a href="/wiki/Mfecane" title="Mfecane">Mfecane</a> period, 1823–1843, when a succession of invading peoples from South Africa entered the country. Although the Bangwaketse were able to defeat the invading <a href="/wiki/Makololo_tribe" class="mw-redirect" title="Makololo tribe">Bakololo</a> in 1826, over time all the major chiefdoms in Botswana were attacked, weakened, and impoverished. The Bakololo and <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ndebele_people" title="Northern Ndebele people">AmaNdebele</a> raided repeatedly and took large numbers of cattle, women, and children from the Batswana—most of whom were driven into the desert or sanctuary areas such as hilltops and caves. Only after 1843, when the Amandebele moved into western Zimbabwe, did this threat subside.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Sechele_Gustav_Fritsch_1865.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Sechele_Gustav_Fritsch_1865.jpg/170px-Sechele_Gustav_Fritsch_1865.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Sechele_Gustav_Fritsch_1865.jpg/255px-Sechele_Gustav_Fritsch_1865.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Sechele_Gustav_Fritsch_1865.jpg/340px-Sechele_Gustav_Fritsch_1865.jpg 2x" data-file-width="592" data-file-height="790"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Sechele_Gustav_Fritsch_1865.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Sechele_I" title="Sechele I">Sechele I</a> who led a Batswana Merafe Coalition against Boers in 1852
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>During the 1840s and 1850s trade with <a href="/wiki/Cape_Colony" title="Cape Colony">Cape Colony</a>-based merchants opened up and enabled the <a href="/wiki/Batswana" class="mw-redirect" title="Batswana">Batswana</a> chiefdoms to rebuild. The Bakwena, Bangwaketse, Bangwato and Batawana cooperated to control the lucrative ivory trade and then used the proceeds to import horses and guns, which in turn enabled them to establish control over what is now Botswana. This process was largely complete by 1880, and thus the Bushmen, the Kalanga, the Bakgalagadi, and other current minorities were subjugated by the Batswana.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Following the <a href="/wiki/Great_Trek" title="Great Trek">Great Trek</a>, <a href="/wiki/Afrikaners" title="Afrikaners">Afrikaners</a> from the Cape Colony established themselves on the borders of Botswana in the <a href="/wiki/South_African_Republic" title="South African Republic">Transvaal</a>. In 1852 a coalition of <a href="/wiki/Tswana_people" title="Tswana people">Tswana</a> chiefdoms led by <a href="/wiki/Sechele_I" title="Sechele I">Sechele I</a> defeated Afrikaner incursions at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Dimawe" title="Battle of Dimawe">Battle of Dimawe</a> and, after about eight years of intermittent tensions and hostilities, eventually came to a peace agreement in Potchefstroom in 1860. From that point on, the modern-day border between South Africa and Botswana was agreed on, and the Afrikaners and Batswana traded and worked together comparatively peacefully.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 1884 Batawana, a northern based Tswana clan's cavalry under the command of Kgosi Moremi fought and defeated the Ndebele's invasion of northern Botswana at the Battle of Khutiyabasadi. This blow to the larger invading Ndebele force signalled the start of the collapse of the Ndebele Kingdom in Zimbabwe and helped galvanize Tswana speaking authority of the area now making part of northern Botswana.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Due to newly peaceful conditions, trade thrived between 1860 and 1880. Taking advantage of this were Christian <a href="/wiki/Missionary" title="Missionary">missionaries</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Lutherans" class="mw-redirect" title="Lutherans">Lutherans</a> and the <a href="/wiki/London_Missionary_Society" title="London Missionary Society">London Missionary Society</a> both became established in the country by 1856. By 1880 every major village had a resident missionary, and their influence slowly became felt. <a href="/wiki/Khama_III" title="Khama III">Khama III</a> (reigned 1875–1923) was the first of the Tswana chiefs to make Christianity a state religion and changed a great deal of Tswana customary law as a result. Christianity became the de facto official religion in all the chiefdoms by World War I.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Colonialism_and_the_Bechuanaland_Protectorate">Colonialism and the Bechuanaland Protectorate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Botswana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Colonialism and the Bechuanaland Protectorate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Bechuanaland_Protectorate" title="Bechuanaland Protectorate">Bechuanaland Protectorate</a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:3_Dikgosi.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/3_Dikgosi.jpg/220px-3_Dikgosi.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/3_Dikgosi.jpg/330px-3_Dikgosi.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/3_Dikgosi.jpg/440px-3_Dikgosi.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3648" data-file-height="2736"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:3_Dikgosi.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>3 Dikgosi <a href="/wiki/Khama_III" title="Khama III">Khama III</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sebele_I" title="Sebele I">Sebele I</a> &amp; <a href="/wiki/Bathoen_I" title="Bathoen I">Bathoen I</a> who negotiated a Protectorate
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>During the <a href="/wiki/Scramble_for_Africa" title="Scramble for Africa">Scramble for Africa</a> the territory of Botswana was coveted by both the <a href="/wiki/German_Empire" title="German Empire">German Empire</a> and Britain. During the <a href="/wiki/Berlin_Conference" title="Berlin Conference">Berlin Conference</a>, Britain decided to annex Botswana in order to safeguard the Road to the North and thus connect the Cape Colony to its territories further north. It unilaterally annexed Tswana territories in January 1885 and then sent the <a href="/wiki/Warren_Expedition" class="mw-redirect" title="Warren Expedition">Warren Expedition</a> north to consolidate control over the area and convince the chiefs to accept British overrule. Despite their misgivings, they eventually acquiesced to this <i><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_French_expressions_in_English#Fait_accompli" title="Glossary of French expressions in English">fait accompli</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 1890 areas north of 22 degrees were added to the new <a href="/wiki/Bechuanaland_Protectorate" title="Bechuanaland Protectorate">Bechuanaland Protectorate</a>. During the 1890s the new territory was divided into eight different reserves, with fairly small amounts of land being left as freehold for white <a href="/wiki/Settlers" class="mw-redirect" title="Settlers">settlers</a>. During the early 1890s, the British government decided to hand over the Bechuanaland Protectorate to the <a href="/wiki/British_South_Africa_Company" title="British South Africa Company">British South Africa Company</a>. This plan, which was well on its way to fruition despite the entreaties of Tswana leaders who toured England in protest, was eventually foiled by the failure of the <a href="/wiki/Jameson_Raid" title="Jameson Raid">Jameson Raid</a> in January 1896.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:1960_6d_Bechuanaland_Protectorate_stamp.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/1960_6d_Bechuanaland_Protectorate_stamp.jpg/220px-1960_6d_Bechuanaland_Protectorate_stamp.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="161" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/1960_6d_Bechuanaland_Protectorate_stamp.jpg/330px-1960_6d_Bechuanaland_Protectorate_stamp.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/1960_6d_Bechuanaland_Protectorate_stamp.jpg/440px-1960_6d_Bechuanaland_Protectorate_stamp.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1172" data-file-height="856"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:1960_6d_Bechuanaland_Protectorate_stamp.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Stamp of <a href="/wiki/Bechuanaland_Protectorate" title="Bechuanaland Protectorate">British Bechuanaland</a> from 1960
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>When the <a href="/wiki/Union_of_South_Africa" title="Union of South Africa">Union of South Africa</a> was formed in 1910 from the main British colonies in the region, the High Commission Territories – the Bechuanaland Protectorate, <a href="/wiki/Basutoland" title="Basutoland">Basutoland</a> (now <a href="/wiki/Lesotho" title="Lesotho">Lesotho</a>), and <a href="/wiki/Swaziland" class="mw-redirect" title="Swaziland">Swaziland</a> (now <a href="/wiki/Eswatini" title="Eswatini">Eswatini</a>) — were not included, but provision was made for their later incorporation. However, the UK began to consult with their inhabitants as to their wishes. Although successive South African governments sought to have the territories transferred to their jurisdiction, the UK kept delaying; subsequently, it never occurred. The election of the <a href="/wiki/National_Party_(South_Africa)" title="National Party (South Africa)">Nationalist</a> government in 1948, which instituted <a href="/wiki/Apartheid" title="Apartheid">apartheid</a>, and South Africa's withdrawal from the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">Commonwealth</a> in 1961, ended any prospect of the UK or these territories agreeing to incorporation into South Africa.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>An expansion of British central authority and the evolution of native government resulted in the 1920 establishment of two advisory councils to represent both Africans and Europeans.<sup id="cite_ref-EISA_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EISA-50">[50]</a></sup> The African Council consisted of the eight heads of the Tswana tribes and some elected members.<sup id="cite_ref-EISA_50-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EISA-50">[50]</a></sup> Proclamations in 1934 regulated tribal rule and powers. A European-African advisory council was formed in 1951, and the 1961 constitution established a consultative legislative council. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Independence">Independence</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Botswana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Independence">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Independence_Day_(Botswana)" title="Independence Day (Botswana)">Independence Day (Botswana)</a>
      </div> 
      <p>In June 1964, the United Kingdom accepted proposals for a democratic self-government in Botswana. An independence conference was held in London in February 1966.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> The seat of government was moved in 1965 from <a href="/wiki/Mahikeng" title="Mahikeng">Mahikeng</a> in South Africa, to the newly established <a href="/wiki/Gaborone" title="Gaborone">Gaborone</a>, which is located near Botswana's border with South Africa. Based on the 1965 constitution, the country held its first general elections under universal suffrage and gained independence on 30 September 1966.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Seretse_Khama" title="Seretse Khama">Seretse Khama</a>, a leader in the independence movement and the legitimate claimant to the <a href="/wiki/Bamangwato" class="mw-redirect" title="Bamangwato">Ngwato</a> chiefship, was elected as the first President, and subsequently re-elected twice. </p>
      <p>The presidency passed to the sitting vice-president, <a href="/wiki/Quett_Masire" title="Quett Masire">Quett Masire</a>, who was elected in his own right in 1984 and re-elected in 1989 and 1994. Masire retired from office in 1998. He was succeeded by <a href="/wiki/Festus_Mogae" title="Festus Mogae">Festus Mogae</a>, who was elected in his own right in 1999 and re-elected in 2004. The presidency passed in 2008 to <a href="/wiki/Ian_Khama" title="Ian Khama">Ian Khama</a> (son of the first President), who had been serving as Mogae's vice-president since resigning his position in 1998 as Commander of the <a href="/wiki/Botswana_Defence_Force" title="Botswana Defence Force">Botswana Defence Force</a> to take up this civilian role. On 1 April 2018 <a href="/wiki/Mokgweetsi_Masisi" title="Mokgweetsi Masisi">Mokgweetsi Eric Keabetswe Masisi</a> was sworn in as the 5th President of Botswana succeeding Ian Khama. He represents the <a href="/wiki/Botswana_Democratic_Party" title="Botswana Democratic Party">Botswana Democratic Party</a>, which has also won a majority in every parliamentary election since independence. All the previous presidents have also represented the same party.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>A long-running dispute over the northern border with <a href="/wiki/Namibia" title="Namibia">Namibia</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Caprivi_Strip" title="Caprivi Strip">Caprivi Strip</a> was the subject of a ruling by the <a href="/wiki/International_Court_of_Justice" title="International Court of Justice">International Court of Justice</a> in December 1999. It ruled that <a href="/wiki/Kasikili_Island" class="mw-redirect" title="Kasikili Island">Kasikili Island</a> belongs to Botswana.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Botswana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Botswana" title="Geography of Botswana">Geography of Botswana</a> and <a href="/wiki/Climate_of_Botswana" class="mw-redirect" title="Climate of Botswana">Climate of Botswana</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Botswana_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Botswana_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg/220px-Botswana_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="220" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Botswana_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg/330px-Botswana_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Botswana_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg/440px-Botswana_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1900" data-file-height="1900"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Botswana_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Botswana map of <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">Köppen climate classification</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>At 581,730&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup> (224,607&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi) Botswana is the world's 48th-largest country. It is similar in size to Madagascar or France. It lies between latitudes 17° and 27° south, and longitudes 20° and 30° east. </p>
      <p>Botswana is predominantly flat, tending toward gently rolling <a href="/wiki/Plateau" title="Plateau">tableland</a>. Botswana is dominated by the <a href="/wiki/Kalahari_Desert" title="Kalahari Desert">Kalahari Desert</a>, which covers up to 70% of its land surface. The <a href="/wiki/Okavango_Delta" title="Okavango Delta">Okavango Delta</a>, one of the world's largest inland <a href="/wiki/River_deltas" class="mw-redirect" title="River deltas">river deltas</a>, is in the north-west. The <a href="/wiki/Makgadikgadi_Pan" title="Makgadikgadi Pan">Makgadikgadi Pan</a>, a large <a href="/wiki/Salt_pan_(geology)" title="Salt pan (geology)">salt pan</a>, lies in the north. </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Limpopo_River" title="Limpopo River">Limpopo River</a> Basin, the major landform of all of southern Africa, lies partly in Botswana, with the basins of its tributaries, the <a href="/wiki/Notwane_River" title="Notwane River">Notwane</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bonwapitse_River" title="Bonwapitse River">Bonwapitse</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mahalapye" title="Mahalapye">Mahalapye</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lotsane_River" title="Lotsane River">Lotsane</a>, <a href="/wiki/Motloutse_River" title="Motloutse River">Motloutse</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Shashe_River" title="Shashe River">Shashe</a>, located in the eastern part of the country. The Notwane provides water to the capital through the <a href="/wiki/Gaborone_Dam" title="Gaborone Dam">Gaborone Dam</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Cuando_River" title="Cuando River">Chobe River</a> lies to the north, providing a boundary between Botswana and Namibia's <a href="/wiki/Zambezi_Region" title="Zambezi Region">Zambezi Region</a>. The Chobe River meets with the <a href="/wiki/Zambezi" title="Zambezi">Zambezi River</a> at a place called <a href="/wiki/Kazungula" title="Kazungula">Kazungula</a> (meaning a small <a href="/wiki/Sausage_tree" class="mw-redirect" title="Sausage tree">sausage tree</a>, a point where <a href="/wiki/Sebitwane" class="mw-redirect" title="Sebitwane">Sebitwane</a> and his <a href="/wiki/Makololo" class="mw-redirect" title="Makololo">Makololo tribe</a> crossed the Zambezi into Zambia). </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ecology">Ecology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Botswana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Ecology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Cebras_de_Burchell_(Equus_quagga_burchellii),_vista_a%C3%A9rea_del_delta_del_Okavango,_Botsuana,_2018-08-01,_DD_28.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Cebras_de_Burchell_%28Equus_quagga_burchellii%29%2C_vista_a%C3%A9rea_del_delta_del_Okavango%2C_Botsuana%2C_2018-08-01%2C_DD_28.jpg/220px-Cebras_de_Burchell_%28Equus_quagga_burchellii%29%2C_vista_a%C3%A9rea_del_delta_del_Okavango%2C_Botsuana%2C_2018-08-01%2C_DD_28.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Cebras_de_Burchell_%28Equus_quagga_burchellii%29%2C_vista_a%C3%A9rea_del_delta_del_Okavango%2C_Botsuana%2C_2018-08-01%2C_DD_28.jpg/330px-Cebras_de_Burchell_%28Equus_quagga_burchellii%29%2C_vista_a%C3%A9rea_del_delta_del_Okavango%2C_Botsuana%2C_2018-08-01%2C_DD_28.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Cebras_de_Burchell_%28Equus_quagga_burchellii%29%2C_vista_a%C3%A9rea_del_delta_del_Okavango%2C_Botsuana%2C_2018-08-01%2C_DD_28.jpg/440px-Cebras_de_Burchell_%28Equus_quagga_burchellii%29%2C_vista_a%C3%A9rea_del_delta_del_Okavango%2C_Botsuana%2C_2018-08-01%2C_DD_28.jpg 2x" data-file-width="6213" data-file-height="4148"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Cebras_de_Burchell_(Equus_quagga_burchellii),_vista_a%C3%A9rea_del_delta_del_Okavango,_Botsuana,_2018-08-01,_DD_28.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Zebras roaming the Okavango Basin
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Botswana has diverse areas of wildlife habitat. In addition to the delta and desert areas, there are <a href="/wiki/Grassland" title="Grassland">grasslands</a> and <a href="/wiki/Savanna" title="Savanna">savannas</a>, where <a href="/wiki/Blue_wildebeest" title="Blue wildebeest">blue wildebeest</a>, <a href="/wiki/Antelope" title="Antelope">antelopes</a>, and other mammals and birds are found. Northern Botswana has one of the few remaining large populations of the endangered <a href="/wiki/African_wild_dog" title="African wild dog">African wild dog</a>. <a href="/wiki/Chobe_National_Park" title="Chobe National Park">Chobe National Park</a>, found in the <a href="/wiki/Chobe_District" title="Chobe District">Chobe District</a>, has the world's largest concentration of <a href="/wiki/African_bush_elephant" title="African bush elephant">African elephants</a>. The park covers about 11,000&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup> (4,247&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi) and supports about 350 species of birds. </p>
      <p>The Chobe National Park and <a href="/wiki/Moremi_Game_Reserve" title="Moremi Game Reserve">Moremi Game Reserve</a> (in the Okavango Delta) are major tourist destinations. Other reserves include the <a href="/wiki/Central_Kalahari_Game_Reserve" title="Central Kalahari Game Reserve">Central Kalahari Game Reserve</a> located in the Kalahari desert in <a href="/wiki/Ghanzi_District" title="Ghanzi District">Ghanzi District</a>; <a href="/wiki/Makgadikgadi_Pans_National_Park" class="mw-redirect" title="Makgadikgadi Pans National Park">Makgadikgadi Pans National Park</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nxai_Pan_National_Park" title="Nxai Pan National Park">Nxai Pan National Park</a> are in <a href="/wiki/Central_District_(Botswana)" title="Central District (Botswana)">Central District</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Makgadikgadi_Pan" title="Makgadikgadi Pan">Makgadikgadi Pan</a>. Mashatu Game Reserve is privately owned, located at the confluence of the <a href="/wiki/Shashe_River" title="Shashe River">Shashe</a> and Limpopo Rivers in eastern Botswana. The other privately owned reserve is <a href="/wiki/Mokolodi_Nature_Reserve" title="Mokolodi Nature Reserve">Mokolodi Nature Reserve</a> near Gaborone. There are also specialised sanctuaries like <a href="/wiki/Khama_Rhino_Sanctuary" title="Khama Rhino Sanctuary">Khama Rhino Sanctuary</a> (for <a href="/wiki/Rhinoceros" title="Rhinoceros">rhinoceros</a>) and Makgadikgadi Sanctuary (for <a href="/wiki/Flamingo" title="Flamingo">flamingos</a>). They are both located in Central District. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Environmental_problems">Environmental problems</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Botswana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Environmental problems">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r978413945/mw-parser-output/.tmulti">
      <div class="thumb tmulti tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:204px;max-width:204px">
        <div class="trow">
         <div class="tsingle" style="width:202px;max-width:202px">
          <div class="thumbimage">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Okavango_Delta,_Botswana_(2674364913).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Okavango_Delta%2C_Botswana_%282674364913%29.jpg/200px-Okavango_Delta%2C_Botswana_%282674364913%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="133" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Okavango_Delta%2C_Botswana_%282674364913%29.jpg/300px-Okavango_Delta%2C_Botswana_%282674364913%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Okavango_Delta%2C_Botswana_%282674364913%29.jpg/400px-Okavango_Delta%2C_Botswana_%282674364913%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3008" data-file-height="2000"></a>
          </div>
         </div>
        </div>
        <div class="trow">
         <div class="tsingle" style="width:202px;max-width:202px">
          <div class="thumbimage">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Giraffe_crossing_a_road_in_Botswana.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Giraffe_crossing_a_road_in_Botswana.jpg/200px-Giraffe_crossing_a_road_in_Botswana.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="133" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Giraffe_crossing_a_road_in_Botswana.jpg/300px-Giraffe_crossing_a_road_in_Botswana.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Giraffe_crossing_a_road_in_Botswana.jpg/400px-Giraffe_crossing_a_road_in_Botswana.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3008" data-file-height="2000"></a>
          </div>
          <div class="thumbcaption">
           The <a href="/wiki/Okavango_Delta" title="Okavango Delta">Okavango Delta</a> (top)
           <br>Giraffe crossing a road (bottom).
          </div>
         </div>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Botswana faces two major <a href="/wiki/Natural_environment" title="Natural environment">environmental</a> problems, drought and <a href="/wiki/Desertification" title="Desertification">desertification</a>, which are heavily linked. Three-quarters of the country's human and animal populations depend on groundwater due to drought. <a href="/wiki/Groundwater" title="Groundwater">Groundwater</a> use through deep borehole drilling has somewhat eased the effects of drought. Surface water is scarce in Botswana and less than 5% of the agriculture in the country is sustainable by rainfall. In the remaining 95% of the country, raising livestock is the primary source of rural income. Approximately 71% of the country's land is used for communal grazing, which has been a major cause of the desertification and the accelerating soil erosion of the country.<sup id="cite_ref-rala.is_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rala.is-55">[55]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Since raising livestock has been profitable for the people of Botswana, they continue to exploit the land with dramatically increasing numbers of animals. From 1966 to 1991, the livestock population grew from 1.7 million to 5.5 million.<sup id="cite_ref-rala.is_55-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rala.is-55">[55]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>64</span></sup> Similarly, the human population has increased from 574,000 in 1971 to 1.5 million in 1995, a 161% increase in 24 years. "Over 50% of all households in Botswana own cattle, which is currently the largest single source of rural income." "Rangeland degradation or desertification is regarded as the reduction in land productivity as a result of overstocking and overgrazing, or as a result of veld product gathering for commercial use. Degradation is exacerbated by the effects of drought and climate change."<sup id="cite_ref-rala.is_55-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rala.is-55">[55]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Environmentalists report that the <a href="/wiki/Okavango_Delta" title="Okavango Delta">Okavango Delta</a> is drying up due to the increased grazing of livestock.<sup id="cite_ref-afrol.com_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-afrol.com-56">[56]</a></sup> The Okavango Delta is one of the major semi-forested wetlands in Botswana and one of the largest inland deltas in the world; it is a crucial ecosystem to the survival of many animals.<sup id="cite_ref-afrol.com_56-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-afrol.com-56">[56]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The Department of Forestry and Range Resources has already begun to implement a project to reintroduce indigenous vegetation into communities in Kgalagadi South, Kweneng North and Boteti.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup> Reintroduction of indigenous vegetation will help reduce the degradation of the land. The <a href="/wiki/United_States_Government" class="mw-redirect" title="United States Government">United States Government</a> has also entered into an agreement with Botswana, giving them US$7 million to reduce Botswana's debt by US$8.3 million. The stipulation of the US reducing Botswana's debt is that Botswana will focus on more extensive <a href="/wiki/Conservation_biology" title="Conservation biology">conservation</a> of the land.<sup id="cite_ref-afrol.com_56-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-afrol.com-56">[56]</a></sup> The country had a 2018 <a href="/wiki/Forest_Landscape_Integrity_Index" title="Forest Landscape Integrity Index">Forest Landscape Integrity Index</a> mean score of 9.13/10, ranking it 8th globally out of 172 countries.<sup id="cite_ref-FLII-Supplementary_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FLII-Supplementary-58">[58]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Development_Programme" title="United Nations Development Programme">United Nations Development Programme</a> claims that poverty is a major problem behind the <a href="/wiki/Overexploitation" title="Overexploitation">overexploitation</a> of resources, including land, in Botswana. To help change this the UNDP joined in with a project started in the southern community of Struizendam in Botswana. The purpose of the project is to draw from "indigenous knowledge and traditional land management systems". The leaders of this movement are supposed to be the people in the community, to draw them in, in turn increasing their possibilities to earn an income and thus decreasing poverty. The UNDP also stated that the government has to effectively implement policies to allow people to manage their own local resources and are giving the government information to help with policy development.<sup id="cite_ref-afrol1_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-afrol1-59">[59]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government_and_politics">Government and politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Botswana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Government and politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Botswana" title="Politics of Botswana">Politics of Botswana</a> and <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Botswana" title="Government of Botswana">Government of Botswana</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Mokgweetsi_E.K._Masisi,_President_of_the_Republic_of_Botswana.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Mokgweetsi_E.K._Masisi%2C_President_of_the_Republic_of_Botswana.jpg/170px-Mokgweetsi_E.K._Masisi%2C_President_of_the_Republic_of_Botswana.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="238" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Mokgweetsi_E.K._Masisi%2C_President_of_the_Republic_of_Botswana.jpg/255px-Mokgweetsi_E.K._Masisi%2C_President_of_the_Republic_of_Botswana.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Mokgweetsi_E.K._Masisi%2C_President_of_the_Republic_of_Botswana.jpg/340px-Mokgweetsi_E.K._Masisi%2C_President_of_the_Republic_of_Botswana.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2383" data-file-height="3336"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Mokgweetsi_E.K._Masisi,_President_of_the_Republic_of_Botswana.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The current president, <a href="/wiki/Mokgweetsi_Masisi" title="Mokgweetsi Masisi">Mokgweetsi Masisi</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Botswana is the continent's oldest democracy. The <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Botswana" title="Constitution of Botswana">Constitution of Botswana</a> is the <a href="/wiki/Rule_of_law" title="Rule of law">rule of law</a>, which protects the citizens of Botswana and represents their rights. The politics of Botswana take place in a framework of a <a href="/wiki/Multi-party_system" title="Multi-party system">multi-party</a> <a href="/wiki/Representative_democracy" title="Representative democracy">representative democratic</a> republic, whereby the <a href="/wiki/President_of_Botswana" title="President of Botswana">President of Botswana</a> is both <a href="/wiki/Head_of_state" title="Head of state">head of state</a> and <a href="/wiki/Head_of_government" title="Head of government">head of government</a>, and is elected by and accountable to the <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_Botswana" title="Parliament of Botswana">Parliament of Botswana</a>. <a href="/wiki/Executive_power" class="mw-redirect" title="Executive power">Executive power</a> is exercised by the government. <a href="/wiki/Legislative_power" class="mw-redirect" title="Legislative power">Legislative power</a> is vested in both the government and the Parliament of Botswana. <a href="/wiki/2019_Botswana_general_election" title="2019 Botswana general election">The most recent election</a>, its eleventh, was held on 23 October 2019. Since independence was declared, the party system has been dominated by the <a href="/wiki/Botswana_Democratic_Party" title="Botswana Democratic Party">Botswana Democratic Party</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Botswana was ranked as a "flawed democracy" and 33rd out of 167 states in the 2020 <a href="/wiki/Democracy_Index" title="Democracy Index">Democracy Index</a>. This was the highest rating in continental Africa (with only the offshore archipelago of <a href="/wiki/Cape_Verde" title="Cape Verde">Cape Verde</a> besting its ranking.) According to <a href="/wiki/Transparency_International" title="Transparency International">Transparency International</a>, Botswana is the least corrupt country in Africa and ranks just below Portugal and South Korea.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Judiciary">Judiciary</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Botswana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Judiciary">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Judiciary" title="Judiciary">judiciary</a> is independent of the executive and the legislature.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>It consists of a typical court system of local Magistrates Courts, a <a href="/wiki/High_Court_of_Botswana" title="High Court of Botswana">High Court</a> and a Court of Appeal. The High Court is a superior court of record with unlimited original jurisdiction to hear and determine any criminal, civil or constitutional cases under any law. Appeals can be heard by the Court of Appeal. The Head of the High Court is the Chief Justice.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The Court of Appeal is the highest and final court in the country and deals with appeals from the High Court and the Industrial Court. The Head of the Court of Appeal is the Judge President. </p>
      <p>Judges are appointed by the President of Botswana on the recommendation of the Judicial Services Commission. </p>
      <p><b>Chief Justices</b>:<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup> </p> 
      <ul>
       <li>1968–1971 John Richard Dendy-Young</li> 
       <li>1972–1975 <a href="/wiki/Akinola_Aguda" title="Akinola Aguda">Akinola Aguda</a></li> 
       <li>1975–1977 George O.L. Dyke</li> 
       <li>1977–1981 <a href="/wiki/Robert_John_Hayfron-Benjamin" title="Robert John Hayfron-Benjamin">Robert John Hayfron-Benjamin</a></li> 
       <li>1981–1987 O'Brien Quinn</li> 
       <li>1987–1992 Livesey Luke</li> 
       <li>1992–1997 Moleleki Didwell Mokama</li> 
       <li>1997–2010 Julian Mukwesu Nganunu</li> 
       <li>2010–2018 Maruping Dibotelo</li> 
       <li>2018–present Terence Rannowane</li>
      </ul> 
      <p>With regard to the legal profession, although the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Law_Society_of_Botswana&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Law Society of Botswana (page does not exist)">Law Society of Botswana</a> has been in existence since 1997,<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> there is still no clear indication in their registry of attorneys as to how certain demographics, such as women, have fared in the legal field. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations_and_military">Foreign relations and military</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Botswana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Foreign relations and military">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:2_BDF_Air_Wing_C-130s_2008-09-12.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/2_BDF_Air_Wing_C-130s_2008-09-12.jpg/220px-2_BDF_Air_Wing_C-130s_2008-09-12.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="133" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/2_BDF_Air_Wing_C-130s_2008-09-12.jpg/330px-2_BDF_Air_Wing_C-130s_2008-09-12.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/2_BDF_Air_Wing_C-130s_2008-09-12.jpg/440px-2_BDF_Air_Wing_C-130s_2008-09-12.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1541" data-file-height="932"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:2_BDF_Air_Wing_C-130s_2008-09-12.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>2 <a href="/wiki/Botswana_Defence_Force" title="Botswana Defence Force">Botswana Defence Force</a> Air Wing <a href="/wiki/C130_Hercules" class="mw-redirect" title="C130 Hercules">C130 Hercules</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Botswana" title="Foreign relations of Botswana">Foreign relations of Botswana</a> and <a href="/wiki/Botswana_Defence_Force" title="Botswana Defence Force">Botswana Defence Force</a>
      </div> 
      <p>At the time of independence, Botswana had no armed forces. It was only after the <a href="/wiki/Rhodesia" title="Rhodesia">Rhodesian</a> and <a href="/wiki/South_African_Army" title="South African Army">South African armies</a> armies attacked the <a href="/wiki/Zimbabwe_People%27s_Revolutionary_Army" title="Zimbabwe People's Revolutionary Army">Zimbabwe People's Revolutionary Army</a> and <a href="/wiki/Umkhonto_we_Sizwe" class="mw-redirect" title="Umkhonto we Sizwe">Umkhonto we Sizwe</a><sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup> bases respectively that the <a href="/wiki/Botswana_Defence_Force" title="Botswana Defence Force">Botswana Defence Force</a> (BDF) was formed in 1977.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup> The President is <a href="/wiki/Commander-in-chief" title="Commander-in-chief">commander-in-chief</a> of the armed forces and appoints a defence council and the BDF currently consists of roughly 60,000 servicemen. In 2019, Botswana signed the UN <a href="/wiki/Treaty_on_the_Prohibition_of_Nuclear_Weapons" title="Treaty on the Prohibition of Nuclear Weapons">treaty on the Prohibition of Nuclear Weapons</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Following political changes in South Africa and the region, the BDF's missions have increasingly focused on prevention of <a href="/wiki/Poaching" title="Poaching">poaching</a>, <a href="/wiki/Emergency_management" title="Emergency management">preparing for disasters</a>, and foreign <a href="/wiki/Peacekeeping" title="Peacekeeping">peacekeeping</a>. The United States has been the largest single foreign contributor to the development of the BDF, and a large segment of its officer corps have received U.S. training. The Botswana government gave the United States permission to explore the possibility of establishing an Africa Command (<a href="/wiki/United_States_Africa_Command" title="United States Africa Command">AFRICOM</a>) base in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Human_rights">Human rights</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Botswana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Human rights">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Human_rights_in_Botswana" title="Human rights in Botswana">Human rights in Botswana</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Many of the indigenous <a href="/wiki/San_people" title="San people">San people</a> have been forcibly relocated from their land to reservations. To make them relocate, they were denied access to water on their land and faced arrest if they hunted, which was their primary source of food.<sup id="cite_ref-bbc1_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc1-70">[70]</a></sup> Their lands lie in the middle of the world's richest <a href="/wiki/Diamond" title="Diamond">diamond</a> field. Officially, the government denies that there is any link to mining and claims the relocation is to preserve the wildlife and ecosystem, even though the San people have lived sustainably on the land for millennia.<sup id="cite_ref-bbc1_70-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc1-70">[70]</a></sup> On the reservations they struggle to find employment, and <a href="/wiki/Alcoholism" title="Alcoholism">alcoholism</a> is rampant.<sup id="cite_ref-bbc1_70-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc1-70">[70]</a></sup> On 24 August 2018 the UN Special Rapporteur on Minorities, Fernand de Varennes, issued a statement calling on Botswana "to step up efforts to recognize and protect the rights of minorities in relation to public services, land and resource use and the use of minority languages in education and other critical areas." </p>
      <p>Until June 2019, <a href="/wiki/LGBT_rights_in_Botswana" title="LGBT rights in Botswana">homosexual acts</a> were illegal in Botswana. A Botswana High Court decision of 11 June of that year struck down provisions in the Criminal Code that punished "carnal knowledge of any person against the order of nature" and "acts of gross indecency", making Botswana one of twenty-two African countries that have either <a href="/wiki/Decriminalization" title="Decriminalization">decriminalised</a> or <a href="/wiki/Legalization" title="Legalization">legalised</a> homosexual acts.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Capital_punishment_in_Botswana" title="Capital punishment in Botswana">Capital punishment in Botswana</a> includes the death penalty by hanging.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The Botswana Centre for Human Rights, Ditshwanelo, was established in 1993.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Botswana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Administrative divisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Districts_of_Botswana" title="Districts of Botswana">Districts of Botswana</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sub-districts_of_Botswana" title="Sub-districts of Botswana">Sub-districts of Botswana</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:242px;">
        <div class="noresize">
         <map name="ImageMap_5a04dc2b35e07714"><area href="/wiki/North-West_District_(Botswana)" shape="poly" coords="42,17,105,17,105,33,130,33,130,67,105,67,105,84,42,84" alt="North-West District (Botswana)" title="North-West District (Botswana)"><area href="/wiki/Chobe_District" shape="rect" coords="151,13,109,33" alt="Chobe District" title="Chobe District"><area href="/wiki/Central_District_(Botswana)" shape="poly" coords="134,38,151,38,180,71,180,100,230,100,180,142,151,142,109,84,109,67,134,71" alt="Central District (Botswana)" title="Central District (Botswana)"><area href="/wiki/North-East_District_(Botswana)" shape="rect" coords="234,67,180,100" alt="North-East District (Botswana)" title="North-East District (Botswana)"><area href="/wiki/Ghanzi_District" shape="poly" coords="42,84,105,84,138,130,134,138,21,138,21,109,42,109" alt="Ghanzi District" title="Ghanzi District"><area href="/wiki/Kweneng_District" shape="rect" coords="151,138,88,159" alt="Kweneng District" title="Kweneng District"><area href="/wiki/Kgatleng_District" shape="rect" coords="226,147,151,172" alt="Kgatleng District" title="Kgatleng District"><area href="/wiki/Kgalagadi_District" shape="rect" coords="92,138,17,218" alt="Kgalagadi District" title="Kgalagadi District"><area href="/wiki/Southern_District_(Botswana)" shape="rect" coords="142,167,109,193" alt="Southern District (Botswana)" title="Southern District (Botswana)"><area href="/wiki/South-East_District_(Botswana)" shape="rect" coords="186,167,142,193" alt="South-East District (Botswana)" title="South-East District (Botswana)"></map>
         <img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Districts_of_Botswana_%28image_map%29.svg/240px-Districts_of_Botswana_%28image_map%29.svg.png" decoding="async" width="240" height="232" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Districts_of_Botswana_%28image_map%29.svg/360px-Districts_of_Botswana_%28image_map%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Districts_of_Botswana_%28image_map%29.svg/480px-Districts_of_Botswana_%28image_map%29.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1434" data-file-height="1385" usemap="#ImageMap_5a04dc2b35e07714">
        </div> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Districts_of_Botswana_(image_map).svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
