        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Botswana's ten districts are: </p> 
      <ul>
       <li><a href="/wiki/Southern_District_(Botswana)" title="Southern District (Botswana)">Southern District</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/South-East_District_(Botswana)" title="South-East District (Botswana)">South-East District</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Kweneng_District" title="Kweneng District">Kweneng District</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Kgatleng_District" title="Kgatleng District">Kgatleng District</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Central_District_(Botswana)" title="Central District (Botswana)">Central District</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/North-East_District_(Botswana)" title="North-East District (Botswana)">North-East District</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Ngamiland_District" class="mw-redirect" title="Ngamiland District">Ngamiland District</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Kgalagadi_District" title="Kgalagadi District">Kgalagadi District</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Chobe_District" title="Chobe District">Chobe District</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Ghanzi_District" title="Ghanzi District">Ghanzi District</a></li>
      </ul> 
      <p>Botswana's councils created from urban or town councils are: <a href="/wiki/Gaborone" title="Gaborone">Gaborone City</a>, <a href="/wiki/Francistown" title="Francistown">Francistown</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lobatse" title="Lobatse">Lobatse Town</a>, <a href="/wiki/Selebi-Phikwe" title="Selebi-Phikwe">Selebi-Phikwe Town</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jwaneng" title="Jwaneng">Jwaneng Town</a>, <a href="/wiki/Orapa" title="Orapa">Orapa Town</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sowa,_Botswana" title="Sowa, Botswana">Sowa Township</a>. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Botswana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Botswana" title="Economy of Botswana">Economy of Botswana</a>
      </div> 
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r978413945/mw-parser-output/.tmulti">
      <div class="thumb tmulti tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:204px;max-width:204px">
        <div class="trow">
         <div class="tsingle" style="width:202px;max-width:202px">
          <div class="thumbimage">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Jwaneng_Open_Mine.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Jwaneng_Open_Mine.jpg/200px-Jwaneng_Open_Mine.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="133" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Jwaneng_Open_Mine.jpg/300px-Jwaneng_Open_Mine.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Jwaneng_Open_Mine.jpg/400px-Jwaneng_Open_Mine.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2592" data-file-height="1728"></a>
          </div>
         </div>
        </div>
        <div class="trow">
         <div class="tsingle" style="width:202px;max-width:202px">
          <div class="thumbimage">
           <a href="/wiki/File:WV_Gaborone_banner_Debswana_HQ.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/WV_Gaborone_banner_Debswana_HQ.jpg/200px-WV_Gaborone_banner_Debswana_HQ.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="29" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/WV_Gaborone_banner_Debswana_HQ.jpg/300px-WV_Gaborone_banner_Debswana_HQ.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/WV_Gaborone_banner_Debswana_HQ.jpg/400px-WV_Gaborone_banner_Debswana_HQ.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3500" data-file-height="500"></a>
          </div>
          <div class="thumbcaption">
           Jwaneng Diamond Mine (top)
           <br> Debswana Main-Mall Office (bottom).
          </div>
         </div>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Since independence, Botswana has had one of the fastest growth rates in per capita income in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> Botswana has transformed itself from one of the poorest countries in the world to an upper middle-income country. GDP per capita grew from $1,344 in 1950 to $15,015 in 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> Although Botswana was resource-abundant, a good institutional framework allowed the country to reinvest resource-income in order to generate stable future income.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup> By one estimate, it has the fourth highest <a href="/wiki/Gross_national_income" title="Gross national income">gross national income</a> at <a href="/wiki/Purchasing_power_parity" title="Purchasing power parity">purchasing power parity</a> in Africa, giving it a standard of living around that of Mexico.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Tree_map_export_2009_Botswana.jpeg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Tree_map_export_2009_Botswana.jpeg/220px-Tree_map_export_2009_Botswana.jpeg" decoding="async" width="220" height="172" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Tree_map_export_2009_Botswana.jpeg/330px-Tree_map_export_2009_Botswana.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Tree_map_export_2009_Botswana.jpeg/440px-Tree_map_export_2009_Botswana.jpeg 2x" data-file-width="1106" data-file-height="864"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Tree_map_export_2009_Botswana.jpeg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Graphical depiction of Botswana's product exports in 28 colour-coded categories.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:GDP_per_capita_of_Botswana,_1950_to_2016.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/GDP_per_capita_of_Botswana%2C_1950_to_2016.png/220px-GDP_per_capita_of_Botswana%2C_1950_to_2016.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="155" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/GDP_per_capita_of_Botswana%2C_1950_to_2016.png/330px-GDP_per_capita_of_Botswana%2C_1950_to_2016.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/GDP_per_capita_of_Botswana%2C_1950_to_2016.png/440px-GDP_per_capita_of_Botswana%2C_1950_to_2016.png 2x" data-file-width="3400" data-file-height="2400"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:GDP_per_capita_of_Botswana,_1950_to_2016.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>GDP per capita of Botswana, 1950 to 2016
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:GDP_per_capita_(current),_%25_of_world_average,_1960-2012;_Zimbabwe,_South_Africa,_Botswana,_Zambia,_Mozambique.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/GDP_per_capita_%28current%29%2C_%25_of_world_average%2C_1960-2012%3B_Zimbabwe%2C_South_Africa%2C_Botswana%2C_Zambia%2C_Mozambique.png/220px-GDP_per_capita_%28current%29%2C_%25_of_world_average%2C_1960-2012%3B_Zimbabwe%2C_South_Africa%2C_Botswana%2C_Zambia%2C_Mozambique.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/GDP_per_capita_%28current%29%2C_%25_of_world_average%2C_1960-2012%3B_Zimbabwe%2C_South_Africa%2C_Botswana%2C_Zambia%2C_Mozambique.png/330px-GDP_per_capita_%28current%29%2C_%25_of_world_average%2C_1960-2012%3B_Zimbabwe%2C_South_Africa%2C_Botswana%2C_Zambia%2C_Mozambique.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/GDP_per_capita_%28current%29%2C_%25_of_world_average%2C_1960-2012%3B_Zimbabwe%2C_South_Africa%2C_Botswana%2C_Zambia%2C_Mozambique.png/440px-GDP_per_capita_%28current%29%2C_%25_of_world_average%2C_1960-2012%3B_Zimbabwe%2C_South_Africa%2C_Botswana%2C_Zambia%2C_Mozambique.png 2x" data-file-width="1055" data-file-height="700"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:GDP_per_capita_(current),_%25_of_world_average,_1960-2012;_Zimbabwe,_South_Africa,_Botswana,_Zambia,_Mozambique.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>GDP per capita (current),&nbsp;% of world average, 1960–2012; Zimbabwe, South Africa, Botswana, Zambia, Mozambique
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20130823203723/http://www.mti.gov.bw/">Ministry of Trade and Industry of Botswana</a> is responsible for promoting <a href="/wiki/Business_development" title="Business development">business development</a> throughout the country. According to the <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">International Monetary Fund</a>, economic growth averaged over 9% per year from 1966 to 1999. Botswana has a <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_economic_freedom" title="List of countries by economic freedom">high level of economic freedom</a> compared to other African countries.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup> The government has maintained a sound <a href="/wiki/Fiscal_policy" title="Fiscal policy">fiscal policy</a>, despite consecutive <a href="/wiki/Government_budget_deficit" class="mw-redirect" title="Government budget deficit">budget deficits</a> in 2002 and 2003, and a negligible level of <a href="/wiki/External_debt" title="External debt">foreign debt</a>. It earned the highest sovereign <a href="/wiki/Credit_rating" title="Credit rating">credit rating</a> in Africa and has stockpiled foreign exchange reserves (over $7 billion in 2005/2006) amounting to almost two and a half years of current imports. </p>
      <p>The constitution provides for an independent judiciary, and the government respects this in practice. The legal system is sufficient to conduct secure commercial dealings, although a serious and growing backlog of cases prevents timely trials. The protection of intellectual property rights has improved significantly. Botswana is ranked second only to South Africa among sub-Saharan Africa countries in the 2014 International Property Rights Index.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>While generally open to foreign participation in its economy, Botswana reserves some sectors for citizens. Increased foreign investment plays a significant role in the privatisation of state-owned enterprises. Investment regulations are transparent, and bureaucratic procedures are streamlined and open, although somewhat slow. Investment returns such as profits and dividends, debt service, capital gains, returns on intellectual property, royalties, franchise's fees, and service fees can be repatriated without limits. </p>
      <p>Botswana imports refined petroleum products and electricity from South Africa. There is some domestic production of electricity from coal. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Energy">Energy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Botswana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Energy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="excerpt-block">
       <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r952607947">.mw-parser-output .excerpt .selflink{font-weight:normal}.mw-parser-output .excerpt-indicator{border-left:3px solid #c8ccd1;margin:1em 0;padding-left:1em}</style>
       <div class="dablink excerpt-hat">
        <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable dablink selfref">
         This section is an excerpt from <a href="/wiki/Energy_in_Botswana" title="Energy in Botswana">Energy in Botswana</a><i><span class="mw-editsection-like plainlinks"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Energy_in_Botswana&amp;action=edit">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></i>
        </div>
       </div>
       <div class="excerpt"> 
        <p><a href="/wiki/Energy_in_Botswana" title="Energy in Botswana">Energy in Botswana</a> is a growing industry with tremendous potential. Botswana has significant reserves of coal,<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup> estimated at over 200 billion tons. No petroleum reserves have been identified and all petroleum products are imported refined, mostly from <a href="/wiki/South_Africa" title="South Africa">South Africa</a>. There is extensive woody biomass from 3 to 10t / hectare. </p>
        <p>Most electric power is generated thermally in installations run by the <a href="/wiki/Botswana_Power_Corporation" title="Botswana Power Corporation">Botswana Power Corporation</a>, a public enterprise established in 1970. Electric generating capacity consists of the 132&nbsp;MW <a href="/wiki/Morupule_Power_Station" class="mw-redirect" title="Morupule Power Station">Morupole coal-fired plant</a>. The 60&nbsp;MW coal-fired plant at <a href="/wiki/Selebi-Phikwe" title="Selebi-Phikwe">Selebi-Phikwe</a> has been closed. Total capacity in 2002 stood at 132&nbsp;MW. Production of electricity in that same year totaled 930&nbsp;GWh. <a href="/wiki/Fossil_fuels" class="mw-redirect" title="Fossil fuels">Fossil fuels</a> were used exclusively. Consumption of electricity totaled 1.989&nbsp;TWh. Coal production in 2002 consisted entirely of the <a href="/wiki/Bituminous" class="mw-redirect" title="Bituminous">bituminous</a> type and totaled 992,000&nbsp;tons. Coal is mined solely at <a href="/wiki/Morupule_Colliery" title="Morupule Colliery">Morupule Colliery</a> by <a href="/wiki/Debswana" title="Debswana">Debswana</a>, mostly for the generation of electricity. The government is considering constructing a coal-fired power plant at the same coal field, which would be designed to export power to <a href="/wiki/South_Africa" title="South Africa">South Africa</a>. Further coal-to-electricity power stations are under consideration <sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup> Recently, the country has taken a large interest in renewable energy sources and has completed a comprehensive strategy that will attract investors in the wind, solar and biomass renewable energy industries. Botswana's power stations include Morupule B Power Station (600 MW), Morupule A Power Station (132 MW), Orapa Power Station (90 MW), Phakalane Power Station (1.3 MW) and Mmamabula Power Station (300 MW) which is expected to be online in the near future. </p> Several companies are prospecting for <a href="/wiki/Oil" title="Oil">oil</a>, but none had been discovered as of 2002. However, <a href="/wiki/Amoco" title="Amoco">Amoco</a> (now <a href="/wiki/BP" title="BP">BP</a>) has studied the possibility of <a href="/wiki/Coalbed_methane" title="Coalbed methane">coalbed methane</a> extraction.
       </div>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Finance">Finance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Botswana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Finance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>An array of financial institutions populates the country's financial system, with pension funds and commercial banks being the two most important segments by asset size. Banks remain profitable, well-capitalised, and liquid, as a result of growing national resources and high interest rates.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Bank_of_Botswana" title="Bank of Botswana">Bank of Botswana</a> serves as a <a href="/wiki/Central_bank" title="Central bank">central bank</a>. The country's currency is the <a href="/wiki/Botswana_pula" title="Botswana pula">Botswana pula</a>. </p>
      <p>Botswana's competitive banking system is one of Africa's most advanced.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (September 2010)">clarification needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Generally adhering to global standards in the transparency of financial policies and banking supervision, the financial sector provides ample access to credit for entrepreneurs.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The Capital Bank opened in 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> As of August&nbsp;2015<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Botswana&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, there are a dozen licensed banks in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> The government is involved in banking through state-owned financial institutions and a special financial incentives program that is aimed at increasing Botswana's status as a financial centre.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Credit is allocated on market terms, although the government provides subsidised loans.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Reform of <a href="/wiki/Non-bank_financial_institution" title="Non-bank financial institution">non-bank financial institutions</a> has continued in recent years, notably through the establishment of a single financial regulatory agency that provides more effective supervision.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup> The government has abolished exchange controls, and with the resulting creation of new portfolio investment options, the <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.bse.co.bw/">Botswana Stock Exchange</a> is growing.<sup id="cite_ref-botswana-facts-figs_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-botswana-facts-figs-86">[86]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Gemstones_and_precious_metals">Gemstones and precious metals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Botswana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Gemstones and precious metals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In Botswana, the Department of Mines<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup> and Mineral Resources, Green Technology and Energy Security<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup> led by Hon Sadique Kebonang in Gaborone, maintains data regarding mining throughout the country. <a href="/wiki/Debswana" title="Debswana">Debswana</a>, the largest <a href="/wiki/List_of_diamond_mines" title="List of diamond mines">diamond mining</a> company operating in Botswana, is 50% owned by the government.<sup id="cite_ref-botswana_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-botswana-89">[89]</a></sup> The mineral industry provides about 40% of all government revenues.<sup id="cite_ref-worldbankbotswana_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-worldbankbotswana-90">[90]</a></sup> In 2007, significant quantities of uranium were discovered, and mining was projected to begin by 2010. Several international mining corporations have established regional headquarters in Botswana, and prospected for diamonds, <a href="/wiki/Gold" title="Gold">gold</a>, <a href="/wiki/Uranium" title="Uranium">uranium</a>, <a href="/wiki/Copper" title="Copper">copper</a>, and even <a href="/wiki/Oil" title="Oil">oil</a>, many coming back with positive results. Government announced in early 2009 that they would try to shift their economic dependence on diamonds, over serious concern that diamonds are predicted to dry out in Botswana over the next twenty years. </p>
      <p>Botswana's <a href="/wiki/Orapa_diamond_mine" title="Orapa diamond mine">Orapa</a> mine is the largest diamond mine in the world in terms of value and quantity of carats produced annually.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup> Estimated to have produced over 11 million carats in 2013, with an average price of $145/carat, the Orapa mine was estimated to produce over $1.6 billion worth of diamonds in 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-Kitco_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kitco-92">[92]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Botswana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Botswana" title="Demographics of Botswana">Demographics of Botswana</a>
      </div> 
      <table class="wikitable" style="float: right; margin-right: 10px"> 
       <caption>
        Population in Botswana<sup id="cite_ref-UN_WPP_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN_WPP-9">[9]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-UN_WPP_2019_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN_WPP_2019-10">[10]</a></sup> 
       </caption> 
       <tbody>
        <tr> 
         <th scope="col" style="background:#cfb;">Year </th> 
         <th scope="col" style="background:#cfb;">Million </th>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td>1950</td> 
         <td style="text-align:right;">0.4 </td>
        </tr>

         <td>2000</td> 
         <td style="text-align:right;">1.7 </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td>2018</td> 
         <td style="text-align:right;">2.3 </td>
        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <p>As of 2012, the <a href="/wiki/Tswana_people" title="Tswana people">Tswana</a> are the majority ethnic group in Botswana, making up approximately 79% of the population, followed by <a href="/wiki/Kalanga_people" title="Kalanga people">Kalanga</a> at 11% and <a href="/wiki/San_people" title="San people">the San (Basarwa)</a> at 3%. The remaining 7% is made up of <a href="/wiki/White_people_in_Botswana" title="White people in Botswana">White Botswanans</a> (3%),<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Indians_in_Botswana" title="Indians in Botswana">Indians</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-cia_1-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia-1">[1]</a></sup> and a number of other smaller Southern African ethnic groups. </p>
      <p>Native groups include the <a href="/wiki/Bayei" class="mw-redirect" title="Bayei">Bayei</a>, Bambukushu, <a href="/wiki/Basubia" class="mw-redirect" title="Basubia">Basubia</a>, Baherero and <a href="/wiki/Bakgalagadi" class="mw-redirect" title="Bakgalagadi">Bakgalagadi</a>. The Indian minority is made up of both recent migrants and descendants of Indian migrants who arrived from <a href="/wiki/Mozambique" title="Mozambique">Mozambique</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kenya" title="Kenya">Kenya</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tanzania" title="Tanzania">Tanzania</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mauritius" title="Mauritius">Mauritius</a> and <a href="/wiki/South_Africa" title="South Africa">South Africa</a>. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Bev%C3%B6lkerungspyramide_Botswana_2016.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Bev%C3%B6lkerungspyramide_Botswana_2016.png/220px-Bev%C3%B6lkerungspyramide_Botswana_2016.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="153" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Bev%C3%B6lkerungspyramide_Botswana_2016.png/330px-Bev%C3%B6lkerungspyramide_Botswana_2016.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Bev%C3%B6lkerungspyramide_Botswana_2016.png/440px-Bev%C3%B6lkerungspyramide_Botswana_2016.png 2x" data-file-width="610" data-file-height="425"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Bev%C3%B6lkerungspyramide_Botswana_2016.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Population pyramid 2016
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Since 2000, because of deteriorating economic conditions in <a href="/wiki/Zimbabwe" title="Zimbabwe">Zimbabwe</a>, the number of <a href="/wiki/Zimbabweans_in_Botswana" title="Zimbabweans in Botswana">Zimbabweans in Botswana</a> has risen into the tens of thousands.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Fewer than 10,000 <a href="/wiki/San_people" title="San people">San people</a> are still living their traditional <a href="/wiki/Hunter-gatherer" title="Hunter-gatherer">hunter-gatherer</a> way of life. Since the mid-1990s the central government of Botswana has been trying to move San out of their historic lands.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/James_Anaya" title="James Anaya">James Anaya</a>, as the Special Rapporteur on the situation of human rights and fundamental freedoms of indigenous people for the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> in 2010, described loss of land as a major contributor to many of the problems facing Botswana's indigenous people, citing the San's eviction from the <a href="/wiki/Central_Kalahari_Game_Reserve" title="Central Kalahari Game Reserve">Central Kalahari Game Reserve</a> (CKGR)<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup> as a special example.<sup id="cite_ref-Anaya_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Anaya-97">[97]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>2</span></sup> Among Anaya's recommendations in a report to the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Human_Rights_Council" title="United Nations Human Rights Council">United Nations Human Rights Council</a> was that development programs should promote, in consultation with indigenous communities such as the San and Bakgalagadi people, activities in harmony with the culture of those communities such as traditional hunting and gathering activities.<sup id="cite_ref-Anaya_97-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Anaya-97">[97]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>19</span></sup> </p>

      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Botswana" title="Languages of Botswana">Languages of Botswana</a> and <a href="/wiki/Setswana" class="mw-redirect" title="Setswana">Setswana</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The official language of Botswana is English although <a href="/wiki/Tswana_language" title="Tswana language">Setswana</a> is widely spoken across the country. In Setswana, <a href="/wiki/Prefix" title="Prefix">prefixes</a> are more important than they are in many other languages, since Setswana is a <a href="/wiki/Bantu_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Bantu language">Bantu language</a> and has noun classes denoted by these prefixes. They include <i>Bo</i>, which refers to the country, <i>Ba</i>, which refers to the people, <i>Mo</i>, which is one person, and <i>Se</i> which is the language. For example, the main ethnic group of Botswana is the Tswana people, hence the name Botswana for its country. The people as a whole are Batswana, one person is a Motswana, and the language they speak is Setswana. </p>
      <p>Other languages spoken in Botswana include <a href="/wiki/Kalanga_language" title="Kalanga language">Kalanga</a> (sekalanga), <a href="/wiki/Tshwa_language" title="Tshwa language">Sarwa</a> (sesarwa), <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ndebele_language" title="Northern Ndebele language">Ndebele</a>, Kgalagadi, Tswapong, <a href="/wiki/Taa_language" title="Taa language">!Xóõ</a>, Yeyi, and, in some parts, <a href="/wiki/Afrikaans_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Afrikaans language">Afrikaans</a>. </p>
