            <div style="background:yellow; width:7%; overflow: hidden;">
              
            </div></td> 
           <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">7%</td> 
          </tr> 
          <tr> 
           <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;"><a href="/wiki/African_traditional_religion" class="mw-redirect" title="African traditional religion">Folk</a></td> 
           <td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;">
            <div style="background:red; width:6%; overflow: hidden;">
              
            </div></td> 
           <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">6%</td> 
          </tr> 
          <tr> 
           <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;"><a href="/wiki/Freedom_of_religion_in_Botswana" title="Freedom of religion in Botswana">Other</a></td> 
           <td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;">
            <div style="background:gray; width:1%; overflow: hidden;">
              
            </div></td> 
           <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">1%</td> 
          </tr> 
         </tbody>
        </table> 
       </div> 
      </div> 
      <p>An estimated 77% of the country's citizens identify as <a href="/wiki/Christians" title="Christians">Christians</a>. <a href="/wiki/Anglicanism" title="Anglicanism">Anglicans</a>, <a href="/wiki/Methodism" title="Methodism">Methodists</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/United_Congregational_Church_of_Southern_Africa" title="United Congregational Church of Southern Africa">United Congregational Church of Southern Africa</a> make up the majority of Christians. There are also congregations of <a href="/wiki/Lutheran" class="mw-redirect" title="Lutheran">Lutherans</a>, <a href="/wiki/Baptists_in_the_United_States" title="Baptists in the United States">Baptists</a>, <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Roman Catholics</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Church_of_Jesus_Christ_of_Latter-day_Saints" title="The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints">The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints</a> (Mormons), the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Reformed_Church" title="Dutch Reformed Church">Dutch Reformed Church</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mennonite" class="mw-redirect" title="Mennonite">Mennonites</a>, <a href="/wiki/Seventh-day_Adventists" class="mw-redirect" title="Seventh-day Adventists">Seventh-day Adventists</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jehovah%27s_Witnesses" title="Jehovah's Witnesses">Jehovah's Witnesses</a> in the country. According to the 2001 census, the country has around 5,000 <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Muslims</a>, mainly from <a href="/wiki/South_Asia" title="South Asia">South Asia</a>, 3,000 <a href="/wiki/Hindus" title="Hindus">Hindus</a> and 700 of the <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%CA%BC%C3%AD_Faith" title="Baháʼí Faith">Baháʼí Faith</a>. Approximately 20% of citizens identify with <a href="/wiki/Irreligion" title="Irreligion">no religion</a>. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Botswana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <p>Besides referring to the language of the dominant people groups in Botswana, Setswana is the adjective used to describe the rich cultural traditions of the Batswana—whether construed as members of the Tswana ethnic groups or of all citizens of Botswana. In Botswana, most of the tribes have different ways to greet one another, but for easy communication and connection, batswana use a three-way hand shake or just greet one another by saying "Dumelang" as a way of saying "hello" without physical contact. In community celebrations like Dikgafela or during marriage ceremonies, batswana women show excitement and happiness by the use of <a href="/wiki/Ululation" title="Ululation">ululations</a> as part of their culture. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Literature_and_cinema">Literature and cinema</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Botswana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Literature and cinema">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Botswana literature belongs somewhere in the strong African literary writing circles. African literature is known for its consciousness and <a href="/wiki/Didacticism" title="Didacticism">didactic</a> writing styles. Writing as an art form has existed in Botswana for a long while, from the rock painting era — especially in the <a href="/wiki/Tsodilo_Hills" class="mw-redirect" title="Tsodilo Hills">Tsodilo Hills</a>, known to be 20,000 years old — to the present day, with the movie production of <i><a href="/wiki/The_No.1_Ladies_Detective_Agency" class="mw-redirect" title="The No.1 Ladies Detective Agency">The No.1 Ladies Detective Agency</a></i>, based on a series of more than 20 novels set in Botswana. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Unity_Dow_-_PopTech_2011_-_Camden_Maine_USA_(cropped).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Unity_Dow_-_PopTech_2011_-_Camden_Maine_USA_%28cropped%29.jpg/220px-Unity_Dow_-_PopTech_2011_-_Camden_Maine_USA_%28cropped%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="204" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Unity_Dow_-_PopTech_2011_-_Camden_Maine_USA_%28cropped%29.jpg/330px-Unity_Dow_-_PopTech_2011_-_Camden_Maine_USA_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Unity_Dow_-_PopTech_2011_-_Camden_Maine_USA_%28cropped%29.jpg/440px-Unity_Dow_-_PopTech_2011_-_Camden_Maine_USA_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2147" data-file-height="1990"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Unity_Dow_-_PopTech_2011_-_Camden_Maine_USA_(cropped).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Unity Dow Author of Far and Beyon, The screaming of the innocent &amp; Heavens may Fall
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In recent times and to date Botswana has seen a remarkable appearance of distinguished writers whose genres range from historical, political and witty story writing. Prominent amongst these are the South African born <a href="/wiki/Bessie_Head" title="Bessie Head">Bessie Head</a> who settled in <a href="/wiki/Serowe" title="Serowe">Serowe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Sesinyi" title="Andrew Sesinyi">Andrew Sesinyi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Barolong_Seboni" title="Barolong Seboni">Barolong Seboni</a> (whose works include <i>Images of the Sun</i>, <i>Screams and Pleas</i>, <i>Lovesongs</i>, <i>Windsongs of the Kgalagadi</i> and <i>Lighting the Fire</i>, and several other publications that include a play; Sechele I, and Setswana Riddles Translated into English), <a href="/wiki/Unity_Dow" title="Unity Dow">Unity Dow</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Galesiti_Baruti&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Galesiti Baruti (page does not exist)">Galesiti Baruti</a>, <a href="/wiki/Caitlin_Davies" title="Caitlin Davies">Caitlin Davies</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Lauri_Kubuetsile&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Lauri Kubuetsile (page does not exist)">Lauri Kubuetsile</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Albert_Malikongwa&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Albert Malikongwa (page does not exist)">Albert Malikongwa</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Toro_Mositi&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Toro Mositi (page does not exist)">Toro Mositi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Moteane_Melamu" title="Moteane Melamu">Moteane Melamu</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Most of Bessie Head's important works are set in Serowe. <i>When Rain Clouds Gather</i> (1968), <i>Maru</i> (1971), and <i>A Question of Power</i> (1973) all have this setting. The three are also autobiographical; <i>When Rain Clouds Gather</i> is based on her experience living on a development farm, Maru incorporates her experience of being considered racially inferior, and <i>A Question of Power</i> draws on her understanding of what it was like to experience acute <a href="/wiki/Mental_distress" title="Mental distress">psychological distress</a>. Head also published a number of short stories, including the collection <i>The Collector of Treasures</i> (1977). She published a book on the history of Serowe, <i>Serowe: Village of the Rainwind</i>. Her last novel, <i>A Bewitched Crossroad</i> (1984), is historical, set in 19th century Botswana. She had also written a story of two prophets, one wealthy and one who lived poorly called <i>Jacob: The Faith-Healing Priest</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-SAHO_101-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SAHO-101">[101]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The 1981 comedy <i><a href="/wiki/The_Gods_Must_Be_Crazy" title="The Gods Must Be Crazy">The Gods Must Be Crazy</a></i> was set in Botswana and became a major international hit, 2000's <a href="/wiki/Disney" class="mw-redirect" title="Disney">Disney</a> production <i><a href="/wiki/Whispers:_An_Elephant%27s_Tale" title="Whispers: An Elephant's Tale">Whispers: An Elephant's Tale</a></i> was filmed in Botswana, starring Hollywood legend <a href="/wiki/Angela_Bassett" title="Angela Bassett">Angela Bassett</a>. Later on, during 2009, parts of <a href="/wiki/M._Saravanan_(film_producer)" title="M. Saravanan (film producer)">M. Saravanan</a>'s Tamil language Indian action film <i><a href="/wiki/Ayan_(film)" title="Ayan (film)">Ayan</a></i> were recorded in Botswana. </p>
      <p>The critically acclaimed <i><a href="/wiki/A_United_Kingdom" title="A United Kingdom">A United Kingdom</a></i>, about the real-life love story of Seretse Khama and Ruth Williams, was filmed partly between Botswana and London, and was released internationally in 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-oxfordbibliographies_102-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-oxfordbibliographies-102">[102]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Botswana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Media_of_Botswana" class="mw-redirect" title="Media of Botswana">Media of Botswana</a>
      </div> 
      <p>There are six <a href="/wiki/Television_station" title="Television station">television stations</a> in Botswana, one of which is state-owned (<a href="/wiki/Botswana_TV" class="mw-redirect" title="Botswana TV">Botswana TV</a>), along with Now TV, Khuduga HD, Maru TV, Access TV and EBotswana. There are five local <a href="/wiki/Radio_broadcasting" title="Radio broadcasting">radio stations</a> (RB1, RB2, Duma FM, Gabz FM, and Yarona FM) and thirteen <a href="/wiki/Newspaper" title="Newspaper">newspapers</a> (<a href="/wiki/Mmegi" title="Mmegi">Mmegi</a>, Sunday Standard, The Telegraph, Business Weekly, <a href="/wiki/The_Botswana_Gazette" title="The Botswana Gazette">The Botswana Gazette</a>, The Voice, The Guardian, Echo, Botswana People's Daily, DailyNews, Tswana Times, Weekend Post, and The Monitor) that publish regularly. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Botswana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Music">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Botswana" title="Music of Botswana">Music of Botswana</a>
      </div> 
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r978413945/mw-parser-output/.tmulti">
      <div class="thumb tmulti tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:204px;max-width:204px">
        <div class="trow">
         <div class="tsingle" style="width:202px;max-width:202px">
          <div class="thumbimage">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Tomeletso_Seeretsi.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Tomeletso_Seeretsi.jpg/200px-Tomeletso_Seeretsi.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="133" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Tomeletso_Seeretsi.jpg/300px-Tomeletso_Seeretsi.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Tomeletso_Seeretsi.jpg/400px-Tomeletso_Seeretsi.jpg 2x" data-file-width="700" data-file-height="467"></a>
          </div>
         </div>
        </div>
        <div class="trow">
         <div class="tsingle" style="width:202px;max-width:202px">
          <div class="thumbimage">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Tswana_Small_Basket.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Tswana_Small_Basket.jpg/200px-Tswana_Small_Basket.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="150" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Tswana_Small_Basket.jpg/300px-Tswana_Small_Basket.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Tswana_Small_Basket.jpg/400px-Tswana_Small_Basket.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4320" data-file-height="3240"></a>
          </div>
          <div class="thumbcaption">
           Folklore Musician Sereetsi (top) &amp; traditional basket (bottom).
          </div>
         </div>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Botswana's music is mostly vocal and performed, sometimes without drums depending on the occasion; it also makes heavy use of string instruments. Botswana folk music has instruments such as setinkane (a sort of miniature piano), segankure/segaba (a Botswana version of the Chinese instrument <a href="/wiki/Erhu" title="Erhu">erhu</a>), moropa (meropa -plural) (many varieties of drums), phala (a whistle used mostly during celebrations, which comes in a variety of forms). Botswana cultural musical instruments are not confined only to the strings or drums. The hands are used as musical instruments too, by either clapping them together or against <i lang="tn-Latn" title="Tswana-language romanization">phathisi</i> (goat skin turned inside out wrapped around the calf area, only used by men) to create music and rhythm. For the last few decades, the guitar has been celebrated as a versatile music instrument for Tswana music as it offers a variety in string which the segaba instrument does not have. The national anthem is "<a href="/wiki/Fatshe_leno_la_rona" title="Fatshe leno la rona">Fatshe leno la rona</a>". Written and composed by <a href="/w/index.php?title=Kgalemang_Tumediso_Motsete&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Kgalemang Tumediso Motsete (page does not exist)">Kgalemang Tumediso Motsete</a>, it was adopted upon independence in 1966.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Visual_arts">Visual arts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Botswana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Visual arts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Botswana" title="Culture of Botswana">Culture of Botswana</a>
      </div> 
      <p>In the northern part of Botswana, women in the villages of Etsha and <a href="/wiki/Gumare" title="Gumare">Gumare</a> are noted for their skill at crafting baskets from Mokola Palm and local <a href="/wiki/Dye" title="Dye">dyes</a>. The baskets are generally woven into three types: large, lidded baskets used for storage, large, open baskets for carrying objects on the head or for winnowing threshed grain, and smaller plates for winnowing pounded grain. The artistry of these baskets is being steadily enhanced through colour use and improved designs as they are increasingly produced for international markets.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECunninghamMilton1987_106-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECunninghamMilton1987-106">[106]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The oldest paintings from both Botswana and South Africa depict hunting, animal and human figures, and were made by the Khoisan (!Kung San/Bushmen) over twenty thousand years ago within the <a href="/wiki/Kalahari" class="mw-redirect" title="Kalahari">Kalahari</a> desert. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Food">Food</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Botswana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Food">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Cuisine_of_Botswana" class="mw-redirect" title="Cuisine of Botswana">Cuisine of Botswana</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The cuisine of Botswana is unique and mostly includes meat as Botswana is a cattle country, the national dish is <a href="/wiki/Seswaa" title="Seswaa">seswaa</a>, pounded meat made from goat meat or beef, <a href="/wiki/Biltong" title="Biltong">Segwapa</a> dried, cured meat ranging from beef to game meats &amp; the cut may also vary, either fillets of meat cut into strips following the grain of the muscle, or flat pieces sliced across the grain. Madila is a popular fermented milk product of Botswana in a yogurt form. Botswana's cuisine shares some characteristics with other cuisine of Southern Africa. </p>
      <p>Examples of Botswana food are: <a href="/wiki/Bogobe" class="mw-redirect" title="Bogobe">Bogobe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pap_(food)" class="mw-redirect" title="Pap (food)">pap</a> (maize porridge), <a href="/wiki/Boerewors" title="Boerewors">boerewors</a>, <a href="/wiki/Samp" title="Samp">samp</a>, Magwinya (fried dough bread) and <a href="/wiki/Imbrasia_belina" class="mw-redirect" title="Imbrasia belina">mopane worms</a>. Porridge (bogobe) is made by putting sorghum, maize or millet flour into boiling water, stirring into a soft paste, and cooking it slowly. A dish called Ting is made when the sorghum or maize is fermented and milk and sugar added. Without the milk and sugar, ting is sometimes eaten with meat or vegetables as lunch or dinner. Another way of making bogobe is to add sour milk and a cooking melon (lerotse). This dish is called tophi by the Kalanga tribe. Many different kinds of beans are grown, including cowpeas, ditloo, and letlhodi. There are some vegetables that grow in the wild that are available seasonally including thepe and Delele (okra). Many fruits are locally available, including marula. Watermelons, believed to have come originally from Botswana, are plentiful in season. Another kind of melon, called lerotse or lekatane, is also grown. There are some kinds of wild melon found in sandy desert areas which are an important food and water source for the people who live in those areas. <a href="/wiki/Kgalagadi_Breweries_Limited" title="Kgalagadi Breweries Limited">Kgalagadi Breweries Limited</a> produces the national beer, St. Louis Lager, Botswana's first and only proud local beer brand that has also been a part of Botswana's rich history since 1989 and non-alcoholic beverage Keone Mooka Mageu, a traditional fermented porridge. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Botswana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sport_in_Botswana" title="Sport in Botswana">Sport in Botswana</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Francistown_Stadium_Botswana.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Francistown_Stadium_Botswana.jpg/220px-Francistown_Stadium_Botswana.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="123" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Francistown_Stadium_Botswana.jpg/330px-Francistown_Stadium_Botswana.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Francistown_Stadium_Botswana.jpg/440px-Francistown_Stadium_Botswana.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4096" data-file-height="2288"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Francistown_Stadium_Botswana.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Francistown_Stadium" title="Francistown Stadium">Francistown Stadium</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">Football</a> is the most popular sport in Botswana, with qualification for the <a href="/wiki/2012_Africa_Cup_of_Nations" title="2012 Africa Cup of Nations">2012 Africa Cup of Nations</a> being the <a href="/wiki/Botswana_national_football_team" title="Botswana national football team">national team</a>'s highest achievement to date. Other popular sports are <a href="/wiki/Softball" title="Softball">softball</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cricket" title="Cricket">cricket</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tennis" title="Tennis">tennis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rugby_football" title="Rugby football">rugby</a>, <a href="/wiki/Badminton" title="Badminton">badminton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Team_handball" class="mw-redirect" title="Team handball">handball</a>, <a href="/wiki/Golf" title="Golf">golf</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Track_and_field" title="Track and field">track and field</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup> Botswana is an associate member of the <a href="/wiki/International_Cricket_Council" title="International Cricket Council">International Cricket Council</a>. Botswana became a member of The International Badminton Federation and Africa Badminton Federation in 1991. The <a href="/wiki/Sport_in_Botswana#Golf" title="Sport in Botswana">Botswana Golf Union</a> offers an <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20130921060147/http://www.botswanagolfunion.org.bw/page2.html">amateur golf league</a> in which golfers compete in tournaments and championships. Botswana won the country's first <a href="/wiki/Olympic_medal" title="Olympic medal">Olympic medal</a> in 2012 when runner <a href="/wiki/Nijel_Amos" title="Nijel Amos">Nijel Amos</a> won <a href="/wiki/Silver_medal" title="Silver medal">silver</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Athletics_at_the_2012_Summer_Olympics_%E2%80%93_Men%27s_800_metres" title="Athletics at the 2012 Summer Olympics – Men's 800 metres">800 metres</a>. In 2011, <a href="/wiki/Amantle_Montsho" title="Amantle Montsho">Amantle Montsho</a> became <a href="/wiki/2011_World_Championships_in_Athletics_%E2%80%93_Women%27s_400_metres" title="2011 World Championships in Athletics – Women's 400 metres">world champion</a> in the 400 metres and won Botswana's first athletics medal on the world level. High jumper <a href="/wiki/Kabelo_Kgosiemang" title="Kabelo Kgosiemang">Kabelo Kgosiemang</a> is a three-time <a href="/wiki/African_Championships_in_Athletics" title="African Championships in Athletics">African champion</a>, <a href="/wiki/Isaac_Makwala" title="Isaac Makwala">Isaac Makwala</a> is a sprinter who specializes in the 400 metres, he was the gold medallist at the Commonwealth Games in 2018, <a href="/wiki/Baboloki_Thebe" title="Baboloki Thebe">Baboloki Thebe</a> was a silver medallist in the 200 metres at the 2014 Summer Youth Olympics and reached the semi-finals at the 2014 World Junior Championships in Athletics &amp; Ross Branch Ross a motorbiker holds the number one plate in the South African Cross Country Championship and has competed at the Dakar Rally. </p>
      <p>The card game <a href="/wiki/Contract_bridge" title="Contract bridge">bridge</a> has a strong following; it was first played in Botswana over 30 years ago, and it grew in popularity during the 1980s. Many British expatriate school teachers informally taught the game in Botswana's secondary schools. The Botswana Bridge Federation (BBF) was founded in 1988 and continues to organise tournaments. Bridge has remained popular and the BBF has over 800 members.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup> In 2007, the BBF invited the <a href="/wiki/English_Bridge_Union" title="English Bridge Union">English Bridge Union</a> to host a week-long teaching program in May 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Botswana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Tertiary_Education,_Research,_Science_and_Technology_(Botswana)" title="Ministry of Tertiary Education, Research, Science and Technology (Botswana)">Ministry of Tertiary Education, Research, Science and Technology (Botswana)</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Botswana" title="Education in Botswana">Education in Botswana</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Lady_Physicist.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Lady_Physicist.jpg/220px-Lady_Physicist.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Lady_Physicist.jpg/330px-Lady_Physicist.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Lady_Physicist.jpg/440px-Lady_Physicist.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2448"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Lady_Physicist.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Physicist in a Lab at <a href="/wiki/Botswana_International_University_of_Science_and_Technology" title="Botswana International University of Science and Technology">Botswana International University of Science and Technology</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Botswana has made great strides in educational development since independence in 1966. At that time there were very few graduates in the country and only a very small percentage of the population attended secondary school. Botswana increased its adult literacy rate from 69% in 1991 to 83% in 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-ref_111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ref-111">[111]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>With the discovery of diamonds and the increase in government revenue that this brought, there was a huge increase in educational provision in the country. All students were guaranteed ten years of basic education, leading to a Junior Certificate qualification. Approximately half of the school population attends a further two years of secondary schooling leading to the award of the Botswana General Certificate of Secondary Education (BGCSE). Secondary education in Botswana is neither free nor compulsory. </p>
      <p>After leaving school, students can attend one of the seven technical colleges in the country, or take vocational training courses in <a href="/wiki/Teaching" class="mw-redirect" title="Teaching">teaching</a> or <a href="/wiki/Nursing" title="Nursing">nursing</a>. Students enter the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Botswana" title="University of Botswana">University of Botswana</a>, <a href="/wiki/Botswana_University_of_Agriculture_and_Natural_Resources" title="Botswana University of Agriculture and Natural Resources">Botswana University of Agriculture and Natural Resources</a>, <a href="/wiki/Botswana_International_University_of_Science_and_Technology" title="Botswana International University of Science and Technology">Botswana International University of Science and Technology</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Botswana_Accountancy_College" title="Botswana Accountancy College">Botswana Accountancy College</a> in Gaborone. Many other students end up in the numerous private tertiary education colleges around the country. Notable amongst these is <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20130904150159/http://www.bothocollege.ac.bw/">Botho University</a>, the country's first private university which offers undergraduate programmes in Accounting, Business and Computing. Another international university is the <a href="/wiki/Limkokwing_University_of_Creative_Technology" title="Limkokwing University of Creative Technology">Limkokwing University of Creative Technology</a> which offers various associate degrees in Creative Arts.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup> Other tertiary institutions include <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20130812002117/http://www.baisago.co.bw/">Ba Isago</a>, ABM University College the largest school of business and management, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.neweracollege.ac.bw/">New Era</a>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20120328065146/http://www.gips.ac.bw/gips.php">Gaborone Institute of Professional Studies</a>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.guc.ac.bw/">Gaborone University College of Law And Professional Studies</a> etc. Tremendous strides in providing quality education have been made by private education providers such that a large number of the best students in the country are now applying to them as well. A vast majority of these students are government sponsored. The nation's second international university, the Botswana International University of Science and Technology, was completed in <a href="/wiki/Palapye" title="Palapye">Palapye</a> in 2011. </p>
      <p>The quantitative gains have not always been matched by qualitative ones. Primary schools in particular still lack resources, and the teachers are less well paid than their secondary school colleagues. The <a href="/wiki/Botswana_Ministry_of_Education" class="mw-redirect" title="Botswana Ministry of Education">Botswana Ministry of Education</a><sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup> is working to establish libraries in primary schools in partnership with the <a href="/wiki/African_Library_Project" title="African Library Project">African Library Project</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Botswana" title="Government of Botswana">Government of Botswana</a> hopes that by investing a large part of national income in education, the country will become less dependent on diamonds for its economic survival, and less dependent on expatriates for its skilled workers.<sup id="cite_ref-UNEVOC_115-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNEVOC-115">[115]</a></sup> Those objectives are in part pursued through policies in favour of vocational education, gathered within the NPVET (National Policy on Vocational Education and Training), aiming to "integrate the different types of vocational education and training into one comprehensive system".<sup id="cite_ref-UNEVOC_115-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNEVOC-115">[115]</a></sup> Botswana invests 21% of its government spending in education.<sup id="cite_ref-ref_111-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ref-111">[111]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In January 2006, Botswana announced the reintroduction of school fees after two decades of free state education<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup> though the government still provides full scholarships with living expenses to any Botswana citizen in university, either at the University of Botswana or if the student wishes to pursue an education in any field not offered locally, such as medicine, they are provided with a full scholarship to study abroad. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Science_and_technology">Science and technology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Botswana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Science and technology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Science_and_technology_in_Botswana" title="Science and technology in Botswana">Science and technology in Botswana</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Botswana is planning to use science and technology to diversify its economy and thereby reduce its dependence on diamond mining. To this end, the government has set up six hubs since 2008, in the agriculture, diamonds, innovation, transport, health and education sectors.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_117-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-117">[117]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Botswana published its updated <i>National Policy on Research, Science and Technology</i> in 2011, within a UNESCO project sponsored by the Spanish Agency for International Cooperation and Development (AECID). This policy aims to take up the challenges of rapid technological evolution, globalisation and the achievement of the national development goals formulated in high-level strategic documents that include Botswana's <i>Tenth National Development Plan</i> to 2016 and <i>Vision 2016</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_117-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-117">[117]</a></sup> The <i>National Policy on Research, Science, Technology and Innovation</i> (2011) fixes the target of raising gross domestic expenditure on research and development (R&amp;D) from 0.26% of GDP in 2012 to over 2% of GDP by 2016. This target can only be reached within the specified time frame by raising public spending on R&amp;D.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_117-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-117">[117]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Despite the modest level of financial investment in research, Botswana counts one of the highest researcher densities in sub-Saharan Africa: 344 per million inhabitants (in head counts), compared to an average of 91 per million inhabitants for the subcontinent in 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_117-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-117">[117]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2009, Botswana-based company Deaftronics launched a solar-powered hearing aid after six years of prototype development. Since then, Deaftronics has sold over 10,000 of the hearing aids. Priced at $200 per unit, each hearing aid includes four <a href="/wiki/Rechargeable_battery" title="Rechargeable battery">rechargeable batteries</a> (lasting up to three years) and a <a href="/wiki/Solar_charger" title="Solar charger">solar charger</a> for them. The product is inexpensive compared to many similar devices, that can start from around $600. <sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2011, Botswana's Department of Agricultural Research (DAR) unveiled Musi cattle, designed to ultimately optimise the overall efficiency for beef production under Botswana conditions. A hybrid of <a href="/wiki/Tswana_cattle" title="Tswana cattle">Tswana</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bonsmara" title="Bonsmara">Bonsmara</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brahman_cattle" class="mw-redirect" title="Brahman cattle">Brahman</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tuli_cattle" title="Tuli cattle">Tuli</a> and <a href="/wiki/Simmental_cattle" title="Simmental cattle">Simmental</a> breeds,<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup> it is hoped that the composite with lead to increased beef production. The objective of the research was to find a genetic material that could perform like cross-breeds already found in Botswana and well above the indigenous Tswana breed while retaining the hardiness and adaptability of the native stock in one package.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:BeeSat_RTM_500x500.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/BeeSat_RTM_500x500.JPG/220px-BeeSat_RTM_500x500.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="220" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/BeeSat_RTM_500x500.JPG/330px-BeeSat_RTM_500x500.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/BeeSat_RTM_500x500.JPG/440px-BeeSat_RTM_500x500.JPG 2x" data-file-width="500" data-file-height="500"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:BeeSat_RTM_500x500.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A Cubesat a type of miniaturized satellite for space research
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In 2016, the Botswana Institute of Technology Research and Innovation (BITRI) developed a rapid testing kit for <a href="/wiki/Foot-and-mouth_disease" title="Foot-and-mouth disease">foot-and-mouth disease</a> in collaboration with the Botswana Vaccine Institute and <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Food_Inspection_Agency" title="Canadian Food Inspection Agency">Canadian Food Inspection Agency</a>. The existing diagnostic methods required highly trained laboratory personnel and special equipment, which caused delays in the implementation of control procedures; whereas the kit developed in Botswana allows for on-site diagnosis to be made.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Square_Kilometre_Array" title="Square Kilometre Array">Square Kilometre Array</a> (SKA) (<a href="/wiki/MeerKAT" title="MeerKAT">MeerKAT</a>) will consist of thousands of dishes and antennas spread over large distances linked together to form one giant telescope. Additional dishes will be located in eight other African countries Botswana among them. Botswana was selected to participate because of its ideal location in the southern hemisphere and environment, which could enable easier data collection from the universe. Botswana government has built SKA precursor telescope at Kgale View, called the African Very Long Base Line Interferometry Network (AVN) &amp; sent student on Astronomy scholarships.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Botswana launched its own 3-year program to build &amp; launch a Micro Satellite (<a href="/wiki/CubeSat" title="CubeSat">CubeSat</a>) Botswana Satellite Technology (Sat-1 Project) in Gaborone on 18 December 2020. The development of the satellite will be lead by <a href="/wiki/Botswana_International_University_of_Science_and_Technology" title="Botswana International University of Science and Technology">Botswana International University of Science and Technology</a> (BIUST) with technical support from <a href="/wiki/University_of_Oulu" title="University of Oulu">University of Oulu</a> in Finland &amp; <a href="/wiki/Loon_LLC" title="Loon LLC">Loon</a>, a giant leap forward in the realisation of Botswana's ambition to become a technologically driven economy. The satellite, which will be used for earth observation, will generate data for smart farming and real-time virtual tourism. Furthermore, it will help us predict and forecast harvest time through the use of robotics and automated technology.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In the <a href="/wiki/IT_sector" class="mw-redirect" title="IT sector">IT sector</a> in 2016 a firm, Almaz, opened a first-of-its-kind computer assembly company.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup> Ditec, a Botswana company, also customizes, designs and manufactures <a href="/wiki/Mobile_phone" title="Mobile phone">mobile phones</a>. Ditec is one of the leading experts in design, development and customisation of <a href="/wiki/Microsoft" title="Microsoft">Microsoft</a> powered devices.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Infrastructure">Infrastructure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Botswana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Infrastructure">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r978413945/mw-parser-output/.tmulti">
      <div class="thumb tmulti tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:204px;max-width:204px">
        <div class="trow">
         <div class="tsingle" style="width:202px;max-width:202px">
          <div class="thumbimage">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Aeropuerto_Internacional_Sir_Seretse_Khama_de_Gaborone,_Botswana.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Aeropuerto_Internacional_Sir_Seretse_Khama_de_Gaborone%2C_Botswana.jpg/200px-Aeropuerto_Internacional_Sir_Seretse_Khama_de_Gaborone%2C_Botswana.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="150" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Aeropuerto_Internacional_Sir_Seretse_Khama_de_Gaborone%2C_Botswana.jpg/300px-Aeropuerto_Internacional_Sir_Seretse_Khama_de_Gaborone%2C_Botswana.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Aeropuerto_Internacional_Sir_Seretse_Khama_de_Gaborone%2C_Botswana.jpg/400px-Aeropuerto_Internacional_Sir_Seretse_Khama_de_Gaborone%2C_Botswana.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3648" data-file-height="2736"></a>
          </div>
         </div>
        </div>
        <div class="trow">
         <div class="tsingle" style="width:202px;max-width:202px">
          <div class="thumbimage">
           <a href="/wiki/File:PSX_20190111_022104.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/PSX_20190111_022104.jpg/200px-PSX_20190111_022104.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="133" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/PSX_20190111_022104.jpg/300px-PSX_20190111_022104.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/PSX_20190111_022104.jpg/400px-PSX_20190111_022104.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4096" data-file-height="2730"></a>
          </div>
         </div>
        </div>
        <div class="trow">
         <div class="tsingle" style="width:202px;max-width:202px">
          <div class="thumbimage">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Francistown_interchange_Botswana.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Francistown_interchange_Botswana.png/200px-Francistown_interchange_Botswana.png" decoding="async" width="200" height="91" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Francistown_interchange_Botswana.png/300px-Francistown_interchange_Botswana.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Francistown_interchange_Botswana.png/400px-Francistown_interchange_Botswana.png 2x" data-file-width="979" data-file-height="443"></a>
          </div>
          <div class="thumbcaption">
           <a href="/wiki/Sir_Seretse_Khama_International_Airport" title="Sir Seretse Khama International Airport">SSKI Airport</a> (top), <a href="/wiki/Air_Botswana" title="Air Botswana">Air Botswana</a> (Middle) &amp; Thapama Interchange (bottom).
          </div>
         </div>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Botswana has 971 kilometres (603&nbsp;mi) of railway lines, 18,482 kilometres (11,484&nbsp;mi) of roads, and 92 airports, of which 12 have paved runways. The paved road network has almost entirely been constructed since independence in 1966. The national airline is <a href="/wiki/Air_Botswana" title="Air Botswana">Air Botswana</a>, which flies domestically and to other countries in Africa. <a href="/wiki/Botswana_Railways" title="Botswana Railways">Botswana Railways</a> is the national railway company, which forms a crucial link in the Southern African regional railway system. Botswana Railways offers rail-based transport facilities for moving a range of commodities for the mining sector and primary industries, as well as passenger-train services and dry ports.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In terms of power infrastructure in Botswana, the country produces coal for electricity and oil is imported into the country. Recently, the country has taken a large interest in renewable energy sources and has completed a comprehensive strategy that will attract investors in the wind, solar and biomass renewable energy industries. Botswana's power stations include <a href="/wiki/Morupule_Power_Station" class="mw-redirect" title="Morupule Power Station">Morupule B Power Station</a> (600&nbsp;MW), <a href="/wiki/Morupule_Power_Station" class="mw-redirect" title="Morupule Power Station">Morupule A Power Station</a> (132&nbsp;MW), <a href="/wiki/Orapa_Power_Station" title="Orapa Power Station">Orapa Power Station</a> (90&nbsp;MW), <a href="/wiki/Phakalane_power_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Phakalane power station">Phakalane Power Station</a> (1.3&nbsp;MW) and <a href="/wiki/Mmamabula" title="Mmamabula">Mmamabula Power Station</a> (300&nbsp;MW), which is expected to be online in the near future. A 200&nbsp;MW solar-power plant is at the planning and design stage by Ministry of Mineral Resources, Green Technology and Energy Security.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-mmegi.bw_132-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mmegi.bw-132">[132]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Health">Health</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Botswana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Health">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="excerpt-block">
       <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r952607947">
       <div class="dablink excerpt-hat">
        <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable dablink selfref">
         This section is an excerpt from <a href="/wiki/Health_in_Botswana" title="Health in Botswana">Health in Botswana</a><i><span class="mw-editsection-like plainlinks"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Health_in_Botswana&amp;action=edit">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></i>
        </div>
       </div>
       <div class="excerpt"> 
        <p>Botswana's healthcare system has been steadily improving and expanding its infrastructure to become more accessible. The country's position as an upper middle-income country has allowed them to make strides in <a href="/wiki/Universal_health_care" title="Universal health care">universal healthcare</a> access for much of Botswana's population. The majority of the Botswana's 2.3 million inhabitants now live within five kilometers of a healthcare facility.<sup id="cite_ref-Health_in_Botswana_:5_133-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Health_in_Botswana_:5-133">[133]</a></sup> The government of Botswana stresses <a href="/wiki/Primary_health_care" title="Primary health care">primary healthcare</a> with an emphasis on <a href="/wiki/Disease_prevention" class="mw-redirect" title="Disease prevention">disease prevention</a> and healthy living. As a result, the infant mortality and maternal mortality rates have been on a steady decline.<sup id="cite_ref-Health_in_Botswana_:3_134-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Health_in_Botswana_:3-134">[134]</a></sup> The country's improving healthcare infrastructure has also been reflected in an increase of the average life expectancy from birth, with nearly all births occurring in healthcare facilities.<sup id="cite_ref-Health_in_Botswana_:5_133-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Health_in_Botswana_:5-133">[133]</a></sup> </p> Access to healthcare has not alleviated all of the country's healthcare concerns because, like many countries in <a href="/wiki/Sub-Saharan_Africa" title="Sub-Saharan Africa">Sub-Saharan Africa</a>, Botswana is still battling high rates of <a href="/wiki/HIV/AIDS" title="HIV/AIDS">HIV/AIDS</a> and other infectious diseases. In 2013, about 25% of the population was infected with HIV/AIDS.<sup id="cite_ref-Health_in_Botswana_avert_135-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Health_in_Botswana_avert-135">[135]</a></sup> Botswana is also grappling with high rates of <a href="/wiki/Malnutrition" title="Malnutrition">malnutrition</a> among children under the age of 5 which has led to other health concerns such as diarrhea and stunted growth.<sup id="cite_ref-Health_in_Botswana_:9_136-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Health_in_Botswana_:9-136">[136]</a></sup>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Health_industry">Health industry</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Botswana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Health industry">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Scottish_Livingstone_Hospital_228.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Scottish_Livingstone_Hospital_228.jpg/220px-Scottish_Livingstone_Hospital_228.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="108" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Scottish_Livingstone_Hospital_228.jpg/330px-Scottish_Livingstone_Hospital_228.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Scottish_Livingstone_Hospital_228.jpg/440px-Scottish_Livingstone_Hospital_228.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1010"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Scottish_Livingstone_Hospital_228.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Scottish Livingstone Hospital in Molepolole
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The Ministry of Health<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">[137]</a></sup> in Botswana is responsible for overseeing the quality and distribution of <a href="/wiki/Healthcare" class="mw-redirect" title="Healthcare">healthcare</a> throughout the country. <a href="/wiki/Life_expectancy" title="Life expectancy">Life expectancy</a> at birth was 55 in 2009 according to the World Bank, having previously fallen from a peak of 64.1 in 1990 to a low of 49 in 2002.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup> After Botswana's 2011 census, current life expectancy is estimated at 54.06 years.<sup id="cite_ref-cia_1-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia-1">[1]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Cancer_Association_of_Botswana" title="Cancer Association of Botswana">Cancer Association of Botswana</a> is a voluntary <a href="/wiki/Non-governmental_organization" title="Non-governmental organization">non-governmental organisation</a>. The association is a member of the Union for International Cancer Control. The Association supplements existing services through provision of cancer prevention and health awareness programmes, facilitating access to health services for cancer patients and offering support and counseling to those affected.<sup id="cite_ref-UICC_Cancer_Association_of_Botswana_139-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UICC_Cancer_Association_of_Botswana-139">[139]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span id="HIV.2FAIDS_epidemic"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="HIV/AIDS_epidemic">HIV/AIDS epidemic</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Botswana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: HIV/AIDS epidemic">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/HIV/AIDS_in_Botswana" title="HIV/AIDS in Botswana">HIV/AIDS in Botswana</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Life_expectancy_in_select_Southern_African_countries_1960-2012.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Life_expectancy_in_select_Southern_African_countries_1960-2012.svg/220px-Life_expectancy_in_select_Southern_African_countries_1960-2012.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="144" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Life_expectancy_in_select_Southern_African_countries_1960-2012.svg/330px-Life_expectancy_in_select_Southern_African_countries_1960-2012.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Life_expectancy_in_select_Southern_African_countries_1960-2012.svg/440px-Life_expectancy_in_select_Southern_African_countries_1960-2012.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="335"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Life_expectancy_in_select_Southern_African_countries_1960-2012.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Life expectancy in several African countries from 1960 to 2012. Botswana had the highest life expectancy until <a href="/wiki/HIV/AIDS" title="HIV/AIDS">HIV/AIDS</a> began to reduce it in the late 1980s.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Like elsewhere in Sub-Saharan Africa, the <a href="/wiki/Economic_impact_of_AIDS" class="mw-redirect" title="Economic impact of AIDS">economic impact of AIDS</a> is considerable. Economic development spending was cut by 10% in 2002–3 as a result of recurring budget deficits and rising expenditure on healthcare services. <a href="/wiki/HIV/AIDS_in_Botswana" title="HIV/AIDS in Botswana">Botswana has been hit</a> very hard by the <a href="/wiki/AIDS_pandemic" class="mw-redirect" title="AIDS pandemic">AIDS pandemic</a>; in 2006 it was estimated that life expectancy at birth had dropped from 65 to 35 years.<sup id="cite_ref-Kallings_140-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kallings-140">[140]</a></sup> However, after Botswana's 2011 census current life expectancy is estimated at 54.06 years.<sup id="cite_ref-cia_1-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia-1">[1]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The prevalence of HIV/AIDS in Botswana was estimated at 25.4% for adults aged 15–49 in 2009 and 21.9% in 2013,<sup id="cite_ref-Gap_21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gap-21">[21]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>A8</span></sup> exceeded by Lesotho and Swaziland in sub-Saharan African nations. This places Botswana at the third highest prevalence in the world, in 2013, while "leading the way in prevention and treatment programmes".<sup id="cite_ref-Avert_22-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Avert-22">[22]</a></sup> In 2003, the government began a comprehensive program involving free or cheap generic <a href="/wiki/Antiretroviral_drug" class="mw-redirect" title="Antiretroviral drug">antiretroviral</a> drugs as well as an information campaign designed to stop the spread of the virus; in 2013, over 40% of adults in Botswana had access to antiretroviral therapy.<sup id="cite_ref-Gap_21-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gap-21">[21]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>28</span></sup> In the age group of 15–19 years old, prevalence was estimated at about 6% for females and 3.5% for males in 2013,<sup id="cite_ref-Gap_21-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gap-21">[21]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>33</span></sup> and for the 20–24 age group, 15% for females and 5% for males.<sup id="cite_ref-Gap_21-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gap-21">[21]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>33</span></sup> Botswana is one of 21 priority countries identified by the UN AIDS group in 2011 in the Global Plan to eliminate new HIV infections among children and to keep their mothers alive.<sup id="cite_ref-Gap_21-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gap-21">[21]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>37</span></sup> From 2009 to 2013, the country saw a decrease over 50% in new HIV infections in children.<sup id="cite_ref-Gap_21-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gap-21">[21]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>38</span></sup> A further measure of the success, or reason for hope, in dealing with HIV in Botswana, is that less than 10% of pregnant HIV-infected women were not receiving antiretroviral medications in 2013, with a corresponding large decrease (over 50%) in the number of new HIV infections in children under 5.<sup id="cite_ref-Gap_21-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gap-21">[21]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>39, 40</span></sup> Among the UN Global Plan countries, people living with HIV in Botswana have the highest percentage receiving antiretroviral treatment: about 75% for adults (age 15+) and about 98% for children.<sup id="cite_ref-Gap_21-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gap-21">[21]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>237</span></sup> </p>
      <p>With a nationwide Prevention of Mother-to-Child Transmission program, Botswana has reduced HIV transmission from infected mothers to their children from about 40% to just 4%. Under the leadership of <a href="/wiki/Festus_Mogae" title="Festus Mogae">Festus Mogae</a>, the Government of Botswana solicited outside help in fighting HIV/AIDS and received early support from the <a href="/wiki/Bill_and_Melinda_Gates_Foundation" class="mw-redirect" title="Bill and Melinda Gates Foundation">Bill and Melinda Gates Foundation</a>, the Merck Foundation, and together formed the African Comprehensive HIV/AIDS Partnership (ACHAP). Other early partners include the <a href="/wiki/Botswana-Harvard_AIDS_Institute" class="mw-redirect" title="Botswana-Harvard AIDS Institute">Botswana-Harvard AIDS Institute</a>, of the <a href="/wiki/Harvard_School_of_Public_Health" class="mw-redirect" title="Harvard School of Public Health">Harvard School of Public Health</a> and the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Botswana-UPenn_Partnership&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Botswana-UPenn Partnership (page does not exist)">Botswana-UPenn Partnership</a> of the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Pennsylvania" title="University of Pennsylvania">University of Pennsylvania</a>. According to the 2011 UNAIDS Report, universal access to treatment – defined as 80% coverage or greater – has been achieved in Botswana.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">[141]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Potential reasons for Botswana's high HIV prevalence include concurrent sexual partnerships, transactional sex, cross-generational sex, and a significant number of people who travel outside of their local communities in pursuit of work. The <a href="/wiki/Polyamory" title="Polyamory">polyamorous</a> nature of many sexual relationships further impacts the health situation. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Botswana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Tourism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Botswana" title="Tourism in Botswana">Tourism in Botswana</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Botswana.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Botswana.jpg/220px-Botswana.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Botswana.jpg/330px-Botswana.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Botswana.jpg/440px-Botswana.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4448" data-file-height="2966"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Botswana.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Tourist on a safari boat cruise
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The Botswana Tourism Organisation<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">[142]</a></sup> is the country's official tourism group. Primarily, tourists visit Gaborone due to the city having numerous activities for visitors. The Lion Park Resort<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">[143]</a></sup> is Botswana's first permanent <a href="/wiki/Amusement_park" title="Amusement park">amusement park</a> and hosts events such as <a href="/wiki/Birthday_party#Birthday_party" class="mw-redirect" title="Birthday party">birthday parties</a> for families. Other destinations in Botswana include the Gaborone Yacht Club and the Kalahari Fishing Club and natural attractions such as the Gaborone Dam and Mokolodi Nature Reserve. There are <a href="/wiki/Golf_course" title="Golf course">golf courses</a> which are maintained by the Botswana Golf Union (BGU).<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">[144]</a></sup> The Phakalane Golf Estate is a multimillion-dollar clubhouse that offers both hotel accommodations and access to golf courses. <a href="/wiki/Museums" class="mw-redirect" title="Museums">Museums</a> in Botswana include: </p> 
      <ul>
       <li><a href="/wiki/Botswana_National_Museum" title="Botswana National Museum">Botswana National Museum</a> in Gaborone</li> 
       <li>Kgosi Bathoen II (Segopotso) Museum in Kanye</li> 
       <li>Kgosi Sechele I Museum in Molepolole</li> 
       <li>Khama III Memorial Museum in Serowe</li> 
       <li>Nhabe Museum in Maun</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Phuthadikobo_Museum" title="Phuthadikobo Museum">Phuthadikobo Museum</a> in Mochudi</li> 
       <li>Supa Ngwano Museum Centre in Francistown</li>
      </ul> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Botswana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r936637989">.mw-parser-output .portal{border:solid #aaa 1px;padding:0}.mw-parser-output .portal.tleft{margin:0.5em 1em 0.5em 0}.mw-parser-output .portal.tright{margin:0.5em 0 0.5em 1em}.mw-parser-output .portal>ul{display:table;box-sizing:border-box;padding:0.1em;max-width:175px;background:#f9f9f9;font-size:85%;line-height:110%;font-style:italic;font-weight:bold}.mw-parser-output .portal>ul>li{display:table-row}.mw-parser-output .portal>ul>li>span:first-child{display:table-cell;padding:0.2em;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .portal>ul>li>span:last-child{display:table-cell;padding:0.2em 0.2em 0.2em 0.3em;vertical-align:middle}</style>

        <li><span><img alt="map" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Africa_%28orthographic_projection%29.svg/28px-Africa_%28orthographic_projection%29.svg.png" decoding="async" width="28" height="28" class="noviewer" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Africa_%28orthographic_projection%29.svg/42px-Africa_%28orthographic_projection%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Africa_%28orthographic_projection%29.svg/56px-Africa_%28orthographic_projection%29.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="550" data-file-height="550"></span><span><a href="/wiki/Portal:Africa" title="Portal:Africa">Africa portal</a></span></li>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="General_sources">General sources</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Botswana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: General sources">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

                   <tr>
                    <th scope="row" class="navbox-group" style="width:1%;font-weight:normal;">Entirely or<br>mostly in Africa</th>
                    <td class="navbox-list navbox-odd" style="text-align:left;border-left-width:2px;border-left-style:solid;width:100%;padding:0px">
                     <div style="padding:0em 0.25em"> 
                      <ul>
